PREFACE 
    This Code constitutes a recodification of the general and permanent ordinances of the Town of Batesburg-Leesville, South Carolina. 
    Source materials used in the preparation of the Code were the 1996 Code and ordinances subsequently adopted by the town council. The source of each section is included in the history note appearing in parentheses at the end thereof. The absence of such a note indicates that the section is new and was adopted for the first time with the adoption of the Code. By use of the comparative tables appearing in the back of this Code, the reader can locate any section of the 1996 Code and any subsequent ordinance included herein. 
    The various sections within each chapter have been provided catchlines to facilitate usage. Notes which tie related sections of the Code together and which refer to relevant state law have been included. A table listing the state law citations and setting forth their location within the Code is included at the back of this Code. 
Title, Chapter and Section Numbering System 
    The title, chapter and section numbering system used in this Code is the same system used in the 1996 Code. Each section number consists of three parts separated by a dash. The figure before the dash refers to the title number, and the figure after the first dash refers to the position of the chapter within the title. The figure after the second dash refers to the position of the section within the chapter. 
Page Numbering System 
    The page numbering system used in this Code is a prefix system. The letters to the left of the colon are an abbreviation which represents a certain portion of the volume. The number to the right of the colon represents the number of the page in that portion. In the case of a chapter of the Code, the number to the left of the colon indicates the number of the chapter. In the case of an appendix to the Code, the letter immediately to the left of the colon indicates the letter of the appendix. The following are typical parts of codes of ordinances, which may or may not appear in this Code at this time, and their corresponding prefixes: 
SPECIAL ACTS SA:1 SPECIAL ACTS COMPARATIVE TABLE SACT:1 CODE CD1:1 CODE APPENDIX CDA:1 CODE COMPARATIVE TABLES CCT:1 STATE LAW REFERENCE TABLE SLT:1 CODE INDEX CDi:1  
Index 
    The index has been prepared with the greatest of care. Each particular item has been placed under several headings, some of which are couched in lay phraseology, others in legal terminology, and still others in language generally used by local government officials and employees. There are numerous cross references within the index itself which stand as guideposts to direct the user to the particular item in which the user is interested. 
Looseleaf Supplements 
    A special feature of this publication is the looseleaf system of binding and supplemental servicing of the publication. With this system, the publication will be kept up to date. Subsequent amendatory legislation will be properly edited, and the affected page or pages will be reprinted. These new pages will be distributed to holders of copies of the publication, with instructions for the manner of inserting the new pages and deleting the obsolete pages. 
    Keeping this publication up to date at all times will depend largely upon the holder of the publication. As revised pages are received, it will then become the responsibility of the holder to have the amendments inserted according to the attached instructions. It is strongly recommended by the publisher that all such amendments be inserted immediately upon receipt to avoid misplacing them and, in addition, that all deleted pages be saved and filed for historical reference purposes. 
Acknowledgments 
    This publication was under the direct supervision of Daniel F. Walker, Code Attorney, and Kayla Mahnken, Editor, of the Municipal Code Corporation, Tallahassee, Florida. Credit is gratefully given to the other members of the publisher's staff for their sincere interest and able assistance throughout the project. 
    The publisher is most grateful to Mr. Ted Luckadoo, Town Manager, for his cooperation and assistance during the progress of the work on this publication. It is hoped that his efforts and those of the publisher have resulted in a Code of Ordinances which will make the active law of the town readily accessible to all citizens and which will be a valuable tool in the day-to-day administration of the town's affairs.

Editorial enhancements include, but are not limited to: organization; table of contents; section catchlines; prechapter section analyses; editor's notes; cross references; state law references; numbering system; code comparative table; state law reference table; and index. Such material may not be used or reproduced for commercial purposes without the express written consent of Municipal Code Corporation and the Town of Batesburg-Leesville, South Carolina.

CHAPTER 1. - GENERAL PROVISIONS 

Sec. 1-1-1. - Form of government. 
    The present governing body of the town shall be that of the council-manager form of government, with a mayor and eight council members. 
(Code 1996, § 1-1-1) 
State Law reference- Requirement for selection of form of government, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-5-10 et seq.; council-manager form of government, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-13-10 et seq. 
CHAPTER 2. - GOVERNING BODY 

Sec. 1-2-1. - Election of governing body. 
    The mayor and council members of the town shall be elected for terms of four years. A general election for town council shall be held every two years to fill those offices available at that time, it being the intent and purpose of this section that the terms of council members be staggered so that not more than one-half of the council and mayor shall be elected in the same general election. 
(Code 1996, § 1-2-1) 
State Law reference- Terms of office of mayor and council members, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-15-40. 
Sec. 1-2-2. - Qualifications. 
(a)  The mayor shall be a qualified elector of the municipality. 
(b)  Each council member shall be a qualified elector and resident of the district he represents at the time he offers for election and during his entire term. 
(Code 1996, § 1-2-2) 
State Law reference- Qualifications of council members, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-15-20; municipal electors, S.C. Code 1976, § 7-5-610. 
Sec. 1-2-3. - Oath of mayor and council members. 
    The mayor and council members, before entering upon the duties of their respective offices, shall take the following oath: 
    "I do solemnly swear (or affirm) that I am duly qualified, according to the Constitution of this State, to exercise the duties of the office to which I have been elected and that I will, to the best of my ability, discharge the duties thereof and preserve, protect and defend the Constitution of this State and of the United States. 
    "As mayor (or council member) of the Town of Batesburg-Leesville, I will equally, fairly and impartially, to the best of my ability and skill, exercise the trust reposed in me, and I will use my best endeavors to preserve the peace and carry into effect according to law the purpose for which I have been elected. So help me God (I so affirm)." 
(Code 1996, § 1-2-3) 
State Law reference- Constitutional oath of office, S.C. Const. art. VI, § 5; statutory oath, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-15-150. 
Sec. 1-2-4. - Compensation. 
    The mayor and council members shall receive as compensation such amount as shall be fixed from time to time by the council, in accordance with state law, and may also receive reimbursement for actual expenses incurred in the performance of their duties. 
(Ord. of 9-10-2018(1)) 
Sec. 1-2-5. - Powers and duties. 
    All legislative powers of the municipality and the determination of all matters of policy shall be vested in the town council, with each member, including the mayor, having one vote. 
(Code 1996, § 1-2-5) 
State Law reference- Powers and duties of municipal council under the council-manager form of government, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-13-30. 
Sec. 1-2-6. - Mayor; emergency powers and duties. 
(a)  In the event of a state of emergency, which shall be deemed to exist whenever, during times of great public crisis, disaster, rioting, civil disturbance, catastrophe or for any other reason, municipal public safety authorities are unable to maintain public order or afford adequate protection for lives, safety, health, welfare or property, the mayor may: 
(1)  Issue a public proclamation declaring to all persons the existence of such a state of emergency; 
(2)  In order to more effectively protect the lives, safety and property of people within the town, define and impose a curfew applicable to all persons, within the jurisdiction of the town, during which it shall be unlawful for anyone subject to curfew to: 
a.  Be or travel upon any public street, alley or roadway or upon public property unless such travel is necessary to obtain medical assistance; 
b.  Possess off one's own premises, buy, sell, give away or otherwise transfer or dispose of any explosives, firearms, ammunition or dangerous weapon of any kind; 
c.  Sell beer, wines or intoxicating beverages of any kind, or possess or consume the same off one's own premises; or 
d.  Sell gasoline or any other similar petroleum products or any other combustible or inflammable substances, except as expressly authorized by the provisions of the curfew imposed; 
(3)  Limit the application of the curfew to any area specifically designated and described within the jurisdiction of the town and to specific hours of the day or night; 
(4)  Exempt from the curfew police officers, firefighters, doctors, nurses and such other classes of persons as may be essential to the preservation of public order and immediately necessary to serve the safety, health and welfare needs of the people within the town. 
(b)  The mayor shall call the town council into session within 24 hours after a state of emergency has been proclaimed and shall proclaim the end of any state of emergency and curfew as soon as circumstances warrant or when directed to do so by the town council. 
(Code 1996, § 1-2-6) 
Sec. 1-2-7. - Mayor pro tempore. 
    At the first meeting of each town council after its election, or as soon thereafter as may be practicable, the council shall elect one of its members as mayor pro tempore. The mayor pro tempore shall be vested with all the powers, duties and responsibilities attached to the office of mayor during the temporary absence or disability of the mayor, or when the office of mayor shall become vacant by reason of death, resignation, removal or permanent disability of the mayor or for any other reason, until a new mayor is duly elected and qualified. Should both the mayor and mayor pro tempore be absent or unable to act, the duties of mayor shall devolve upon and be performed by such member as the council shall designate. 
(Code 1996, § 1-2-7) 
State Law reference- Mayor pro tempore, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-190. 
CHAPTER 3. - RULES OF PROCEDURE AND ORDINANCES 
ARTICLE A. - MEETINGS OF GOVERNING BODY 

Sec. 1-3-1. - Council meetings. 
(a)  Regular meeting. Regular meetings shall be held at 7:00 p.m. on the second Monday of each month. 
(b)  Special meetings/works sessions. Special meetings of the council may be held on the call of the town manager or by four council members presenting a signed request to the town manager detailing the need. Notice of a special meeting shall be given immediately to all available members and the news media by the municipal clerk. Calls for special meetings of the council shall set forth the object or purpose for which the meeting is called and no other business shall be transacted at special meetings. 
(c)  Executive session. An executive session must be set by motion adopted at a regular or special public meeting for at least one reason permitted by the Freedom of Information Act. Council may not take any vote or action in executive session except to adjourn or to return to public session. 
(d)  Remote sites. Teleconferencing, Skype, speakerphone, or any form of audio/visual connectivity presents a challenge in establishing clear connectivity and communication that complies with the mandates of FOIA. Therefore, attendance for council meetings requires a council member's physical presence. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-1) 
Sec. 1-3-2. - Quorum and rules of order. 
(a)  A majority of the members of council serving constitutes a quorum for the conduct of business at any meeting. The mayor shall preside at meetings, or mayor pro tempore in absence of mayor, except that, when both are absent, the members present shall elect a presiding member. A member present but disqualified from voting on a question by state law due to a conflict of interest shall be counted for purposes of a quorum. 
(b)  The mayor or presiding officer shall preserve order and decorum at town council meetings and decide all questions of order. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-2) 
Sec. 1-3-3. - Parliamentary rules. 
    Except as otherwise required by state law or local ordinance, all proceedings of the council shall be governed by Robert's Rules of Order (current edition) and the municipal attorney shall act as parliamentarian. The presiding officer, without debate, will decide questions of order. The decision is subject to appeal of council, with the advice of parliamentarian, to which council can take a vote to override the presiding officer. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-3) 
Sec. 1-3-4. - Agenda. 
    Matters to be considered by council at a regular or special meeting shall be placed on a written agenda prepared by the town manager and publicly posted by the municipal clerk 24 hours prior to the meeting. Matters not on the agenda shall not be considered by council. However, a council member may request during a public meeting of council that an item be placed on the agenda of a future meeting of council. The requested item shall be added to the agenda of the future meeting if approved by a majority vote of council. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-4) 
Sec. 1-3-5. - Order of proceedings. 
    The order of the proceedings of the council shall be as follows: 
(1)  Invocation and Pledge of Allegiance; 
(2)  Approval of agenda; 
(3)  Adopting the minutes of last council meeting; 
(4)  Presentation of awards, proclamations, and resolutions; 
(5)  Reports from department heads and council committees; 
(6)  Public comment regarding items on the agenda; 
(7)  Introduction of ordinances and other business; 
(8)  Reports from executive staff; 
(9)  Potential agenda items for next month's meeting; 
(10)  Executive session; 
(11)  Possible actions by council in follow up to executive session; 
(12)  Adjournment. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-5) 
Sec. 1-3-6. - Recognition of speakers. 
(a)  Every member of the council when about to speak shall address the mayor as "Mr. or Madam Mayor" and in speaking shall avoid all disrespect to the council and all personalities, and shall confine himself to the subject under consideration. 
(b)  The presiding officer, when addressed by a member who rises in order, shall name the member, using no title but that of Mr./Mrs./Ms. The member who shall rise first in order, shall be first heard. If several members rise about the same time, the mayor shall decide who shall speak first. 
(c)  No member shall speak more than twice on the same question without leave of the council, except to explain. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-6) 
Sec. 1-3-7. - Voting requirements. 
(a)  All actions of the council shall be by majority vote of members present at a public meeting. No proxy, mail, telephonic, facsimile, electronic or absentee vote may be cast. 
(b)  Every member of council present, including the mayor, shall vote on every question except when required to abstain from voting by state law. 
(c)  The vote on every question shall be by a roll call or show of hands. 
(d)  The vote on every question shall be recorded in the minutes. 
(e)  No member of the council may leave the council chamber while in public session without permission of the presiding officer. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-7) 
Sec. 1-3-8. - Motions. 
    Motions are to be made orally, and are to be made in the affirmative. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-8) 
Sec. 1-3-9. - Minutes. 
(a)  Minutes must be taken of all public meetings. Minutes are not required of executive sessions and shall not be taken. 
(b)  The municipal clerk shall keep minutes of all public meetings, which shall be a matter of permanent public record. At each regular council meeting the minutes of the previous meeting must be presented for approval. Minutes do not constitute the official record of a meeting until approved by council. A member of council may place a written expression of position on a matter in the minutes no later than the next regular meeting. A written expression must be voted on by a majority of council to reflect a revision of the minutes that include the written insertion. 
(c)  Minutes are not required to be verbatim. Audio and video recordings of each meeting represent a verbatim recording of such events, thereby negating the need for an exact written record. Minutes will reflect the council members in attendance, transactions occurring, record of motions, votes cast, and a synopsis of any discussions. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-9) 
Sec. 1-3-10. - Executive sessions. 
(a)  By majority vote in a public meeting, council may hold an executive session as permitted by the South Carolina Freedom of Information Act, S.C. Code 1976, § 30-4-70. 
(b)  No vote or formal action shall be taken in executive session except to adjourn and return to public session, S.C. Code 1976, § 30-4-70(b). 
(c)  Minutes of executive session will not be taken. 
(d)  It shall be unethical for a member of council or person in attendance to disclose to another person or make public the substance of matters discussed in executive session. Sanctions shall be a vote of council. 
(e)  No audio or visual recording devices shall be used by any member of council or persons present during executive sessions. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-10) 
Sec. 1-3-11. - Code of conduct. 
(a)  Council meetings will be conducted with respect, showing consideration for all in attendance. 
(b)  It is the responsibility of each council member, and the mayor, to be on time and present for every regular or special meeting. 
(c)  Council members who are unable to attend regular or special meetings are to notify the town manager well in advance of the meeting. In an emergency, the town manager must be notified as soon as possible. 
(d)  Council members who arrive after a regular meeting or special meeting has begun shall not interrupt discussions in order to catch up on what has been missed. 
(e)  Cell phones, PDAs, laptops, tablets, or any other form of electronic communication will be turned to silent or off for the duration of all council meetings. Phone calls or texting of any nature is prohibited during council meetings. If a council member must participate in a phone call, in an emergency, that council member must first seek permission from the presiding officer to leave the meeting. 
(f)  The following conduct may be considered disruptive during a meeting and subject the offending council member to sanctions up to, but not limited to, removal from the meeting: carrying on private conversations, speaking out of turn when not recognized by the presiding officer, making frivolous motions, arguing with the presiding officer, making political speeches, involving personalities in comments, making comments not relevant to the business at hand, or refusing to abide by a legitimate ruling of order from the presiding officer. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-11) 
Sec. 1-3-12. - Removal procedure for disruptive actions. 
(a)  The presiding officer must first ask the council member to come to order. 
(b)  If the council member refuses to come to order, the presiding officer must rule the council member out of order. 
(c)  If the council member continues to be disruptive, the presiding officer can order the removal of the council member from the council chambers until council can assess what penalties should be enforced. Penalties include, but are not limited to, allowing the council member to return to the meeting after having had a chance to calm down, censuring the council member, or removing the council member from the remainder of the meeting. 
(d)  Any penalties assessed must be voted on by each member of council. Assessment of penalty will be by majority vote. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-12) 
Sec. 1-3-13. - Appearance of citizens. 
(a)  Any citizen of the municipality may address council at any regular council meeting. Discussion is limited to items on the current agenda. Those who request to speak must sign in with the municipal clerk no later than ten minutes prior to the beginning of the regular meeting indicating their name, address and agenda item on which they intend to comment. Each person who gives notice may speak at a designated time and will be limited to a three-minute presentation at the discretion of the presiding officer. 
(b)  No questions shall be entertained and this is not a forum for debate. Individual council members, and the mayor, may be directly addressed before or after each meeting. The presiding officer may limit the number of speakers. One speaker may not defer his/her allotted time to another speaker. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-13) 
Sec. 1-3-14. - Town manager to attend. 
    The town manager shall attend all meetings of the council unless notification of absence is provided to the presiding officer. In the absence of the town manager, the assistant town manager shall attend. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-14) 
Sec. 1-3-15. - Town attorney to attend; parliamentarian. 
    The town attorney shall attend all regular meetings of council, and special meetings unless excused by council. The attorney shall act as parliamentarian. The attorney shall review all ordinances, resolutions and documents presented to council and give opinions upon questions of procedure, form and law to any member of council. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-15) 
Sec. 1-3-16. - Town clerk to attend. 
    The municipal clerk is the ex officio clerk of council. The clerk shall give notices of meetings, post agendas, attend regular and special meetings, record votes of council, keep minutes of council meetings and perform such other duties as may be assigned by the town manager. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-16) 
Sec. 1-3-17. - Public hearings. 
(a)  Town council shall hold public hearings for those matters required by law and may hold public hearings for any purpose council deems appropriate. 
(a)  Public hearings shall be advertised as required by law, with notices and agenda publicly posted 24 hours before the hearing. 
(b)  A public hearing is understood to be a forum for people interested in the subject matter to present information to town council for its consideration as it deliberates an issue. It is not a forum for debate or argument between members of the council and opponents or proponents, or each other. 
(c)  Each speaker shall be limited to three minutes. The time allowed to any one speaker may be increased or decreased by a majority vote of council. by a majority vote, council may also allow groups of citizens to join together for longer presentations under special circumstances. 
(d)  One speaker may not defer his/her allotted time to another speaker. 
(e)  The presiding officer may terminate a presentation which addresses the same information as presented by a previous speaker to avoid continuous repetition of information. Such speakers shall be encouraged to simply state their agreement with a previous speaker and bring new information to the subject. 
(f)  Public hearings will be held before a regular meeting, but may be held at a time separate from other meetings of town council. 
(g)  Public hearings will be orderly, allowing all who wish to speak to do so without interruption. The presiding officer will take necessary measures to assure all citizens who wish to be heard are allowed to speak. Council members may not speak as an opponent or proponent at any public hearing. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-17) 
Sec. 1-3-18. - Powers and duties in absence of mayor. 
    Town council shall, at the first meeting after installation, elect a member of council as mayor pro tempore. It shall be the duty of the mayor pro tempore to act as the presiding officer in the absence or inability of the mayor from the municipality or when the mayor is incapable of the duties of his office. In the absence or inability of both the mayor and mayor pro tempore, the duties of the mayor shall devolve on and be performed by such council member as the council shall temporarily appoint. Appointment shall be by nomination and majority vote. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-18) 
Sec. 1-3-19. - Investigative powers of council members. 
    By majority vote of council at a properly noticed meeting of council, council members can be granted investigative authority and have the power to inquire into the conduct of any office, department or agency of the municipality, make investigations as to municipal affairs and give the public information concerning them. This does not grant authority for council or any of its members to interfere with daily municipal operations nor shall council or any of its members deal with municipal officers or employees who are subject to the direction and supervision of the manager except through the manager, and neither the council nor its members shall give orders to any such officer or employee, either publicly or privately. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-19) 
Sec. 1-3-20. - Council compensation. 
    Monthly compensation shall be paid monthly at a rate established in accordance with state law by council. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-20) 
Sec. 1-3-21. - Voting. 
    The "yeas" and "nays" of any question shall always be recorded, when required by any member. When the question has been stated, and the first response has been made to the call of the clerk-treasurer, all debate shall cease, and no member shall say more than "yea" or "nay." During the call, no member shall leave the council chamber. Every member present shall, when his name is called, give his vote, unless excused by the council or prohibited by law. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-9; Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-21) 
Sec. 1-3-22. - Reasons for voting may be recorded. 
    Any member of the council may, if he desires, have his reasons for voting for or against any measure recorded on the minutes. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-10; Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-22) 
Sec. 1-3-23. - Interested member not to vote. 
    No member of council shall vote on any questions in which he is personally or pecuniarily (of or relating to money) interested. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-11; Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-23) 
State Law reference- Municipal officers prohibited from contracting with municipality, S.C. Code 1976, §§ 5-7-130, 5-21-30. 
Sec. 1-3-24. - Repeal, suspension, or alteration of rules. 
    Any of the provisions of this chapter pertaining to meetings, rules of order, and conduct of meetings may be suspended at any meeting of the council by a consenting vote of two-thirds of council members present. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-12; Ord. of 11-17-2014, exh. A, § 1-3-24) 
Secs. 1-3-25-1-3-40. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE B. - ORDINANCES AND RESOLUTIONS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Acts of council which are required to be done by ordinance, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-260. 

Sec. 1-3-41. - Ordinances for benefit of town. 
    It shall be the duty of the council to pass from time to time such ordinances as in their judgment shall best promote the interest of the citizens and property holders of the town. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-21) 
Sec. 1-3-42. - Style of ordinances. 
    The style of all ordinances shall be: "Be It Ordered and Ordained by the Town Council of the Town of Batesburg-Leesville, South Carolina, in Council Assembled and by the Authority Thereof." 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-22) 
Sec. 1-3-43. - Introduction of ordinances and resolutions. 
(a)  All ordinances shall be prepared by the town attorney, and introduced in writing and in the form required for final adoption. 
(b)  All ordinances, resolutions, contracts and other documents shall, before presentation to the council, be approved as to form and legality by the town attorney or his authorized representative. 
(c)  Ordinances, resolutions, contracts and other documents that involve substantive matters of administration shall further be examined and approved by the town manager or his designate, after first having been referred to the head of the department under whose jurisdiction the administration of the subject matter would devolve. If the department head does not approve, he shall return the instrument to the town manager with a written memorandum of the reasons why approval is withheld. If the instrument is not redrafted to meet the objection, or if written approval is not obtained, the town manager shall so advise the council. 
(d)  Ordinances, resolutions and other matters or subjects requiring action by the council must be initiated, introduced and sponsored by a member of the council, except that the town attorney may, on his own initiative, prepare and present ordinances, resolutions and other matters or subjects to the council, and any council member may assume sponsorship by moving adoption. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-23) 
Sec. 1-3-44. - Procedure for enacting ordinances; effective date. 
(a)  No ordinance or amendment thereto shall have the force of law until it shall have been read two times on two separate days with at least six days between each reading, and shall have received a favorable majority vote after each reading. 
(b)  Unless specifically provided to the contrary, all ordinances shall take effect and be in force from and after their adoption. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-24) 
State Law reference- Form and procedures for introducing and passing ordinances, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-270. 
Sec. 1-3-45. - Emergency ordinances. 
    Notwithstanding any other provision of this Code, an ordinance to meet public emergencies affecting life, health, safety or the property of the people (but in no event ordinances to levy taxes, grant, renew or extend a franchise or impose or change a service rate) shall have the force of law when adopted by an affirmative vote of at least two-thirds of the members of council present. An emergency ordinance is effective immediately upon its enactment without regard to any reading, public hearing, publication requirements or public notice requirements, and shall expire automatically as of the 61st day following the date of enactment. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-25) 
State Law reference- Emergency ordinances, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-250. 
Sec. 1-3-46. - Ordinances entered in book. 
    The clerk-treasurer shall enter, in a well-bound book, copies of all ordinances passed by the council. The book in which the ordinances are thus entered shall be known as the "Ordinances at Large of the Town of Batesburg-Leesville," and shall be indexed. 
(Code 1976, § 2-23; Code 1996, § 1-3-26) 
Sec. 1-3-47. - Notation of amendment or repeal. 
    The clerk-treasurer shall write on the first page of every ordinance, if the same has been amended or repealed, as the case may be, the words "amended" or "repealed" with a reference to the page of the ordinance book where the amending or repealing ordinance can be found. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-27) 
Secs. 1-3-48-1-3-60. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE C. - USE OF CODE AND PENALTIES 

Sec. 1-3-61. - How Code cited and designated. 
    The ordinances embraced in this and the following chapters and sections shall constitute and be designated "The Code of Ordinances of the Town of Batesburg-Leesville, South Carolina," and may be so cited. Such ordinances may also be cited as "Batesburg-Leesville Town Code." 
(Code 1978, § 1-1; Code 1996, § 1-3-41) 
Sec. 1-3-62. - Definitions and rules of construction. 
(a)  In the construction of this Code and of all ordinances of the town, the following definitions and rules of construction shall be observed, unless inconsistent with the manifest intent of the town council or the context clearly requires otherwise. 
    And, or . The word "and" may be read as "or" and the word "or" may be read as "and," where the sense requires it. 
    Bond . When a bond is required, an undertaking in writing shall be sufficient. 
    Computation of time . The time within which an act is to be done shall be computed by excluding the first day and including the last, and if the last day is Sunday or a legal holiday, that shall be excluded. 
    Council or town council . The term "council" or "town council" means the town council of Batesburg-Leesville, South Carolina. 
    Gender . Words importing masculine gender shall include the feminine and neuter. 
    Month . The term "month" means a calendar month. 
    Number . Words used in the singular number include the plural and the plural shall include the singular number. 
    Oath, swear, sworn . The terms "oath," "swear" and "sworn" shall be construed to include an affirmation in all cases in which, by law, an affirmation may be substituted for an oath, and in such cases, the words "swear" and "sworn" shall be equivalent to the words "affirm" and "affirmed." 
    Owner . The term "owner," applied to a building or land, includes any part-owner, joint owner, tenant in common, joint tenant or tenant by the entirety, of the whole or part of such building or land. 
    Person . The term "person" includes a corporation, firm, limited liability company, partnership, association, organization and any other group acting as a unit, as well as an individual. 
    Personal property . The term "personal property" includes every species of property, except real property, as defined in this section. 
    Preceding, following . The terms "preceding" and "following" mean the next before and the next after, respectively. 
    Property . The term "property" includes real and personal property. 
    Real property and real estate . The terms "real property" and "real estate" include lands, tenements, and hereditaments (heritable property). 
    S.C. Code 1976 . This abbreviation refers to the South Carolina Code of Laws, 1976. 
    S.C. Code Reg. This abbreviation refers to the South Carolina Code of Regulations. 
    Roadway . The term "roadway" means that portion of a street improved, designed or ordinarily used for vehicular traffic. 
    Shall, may . The term "shall" is mandatory. The term "may" is permissive. 
    Sidewalk . The term "sidewalk" means any portion of a street between the curb line, or the lateral lines of a roadway where there is no curb, and the adjacent property line intended for the use of pedestrians. 
    Signature or subscription . The term "signature" or "subscription" includes a mark when the person cannot write. 
    State . The term "state" or "this state" means the State of South Carolina. 
    Street . The term "street" includes avenues, boulevards, highways, roads, alleys, lanes, viaducts, bridges and approaches thereto and all other public thoroughfares in the town, and shall mean the entire width thereof between abutting property lines; the term "street" shall be construed to include a sidewalk or footpath, unless the contrary is expressed or unless such construction would be inconsistent with the manifest intent of the town council. 
    Tenant or occupant . The term "tenant" or "occupant," applied to a building or land, includes any person who occupies the whole or part of such building or land, whether alone or with others. 
    Time . Words used in the past or present tense include the future as well as the past and present. 
    Town . The term "town" means the Town of Batesburg-Leesville, South Carolina. 
    Writing . The terms "writing" or "written" include printing and any other mode of representing words and letters. 
    Year . The term "year" means a calendar year. 
(b)  In the construction of this Code and of all ordinances of the town, all officers, agents, employees and other persons, together with all things and places therein referred to, shall, unless a contrary intention appear, be construed to mean the officers, agents, employees and other persons, things and places situated in the town or employed by or appertaining to the town. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-42) 
Sec. 1-3-63. - Catchlines of sections. 
    The underlined catchlines of the several sections of this Code are intended as mere catchwords to indicate the contents of the section and shall not be deemed or taken to be titles of such sections, nor as any part of the section, nor, unless expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when any of such sections, including the catchlines, are amended or re-enacted. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-43) 
Sec. 1-3-64. - Effect of repeal or expiration of ordinances. 
(a)  The repeal of an ordinance, or its expiration by virtue of any provision contained therein, shall not affect any right accrued, any offense committed, any penalty or punishment incurred or any proceeding commenced before the repeal took effect or the ordinance expired. 
(b)  When an ordinance which repealed another shall itself be repealed, the previous ordinance shall not be revived without expressed words to that effect. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-44) 
Sec. 1-3-65. - Provisions considered as continuations of existing ordinances. 
    The provisions appearing in this Code of Ordinances, so far as they are the same as prior existing ordinances, shall be considered as a continuation of such existing ordinances and not as new enactments. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-45) 
Sec. 1-3-66. - Severability of parts of Code. 
    It is hereby declared to be the intention of the town council that the sections, paragraphs, sentences, clauses and phrases of this Code of Ordinances are severable, and if any phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph or section of this Code shall be declared unconstitutional or invalid by the valid judgment or decree of a court of competent jurisdiction, such unconstitutionality or invalidity shall not affect any of the remaining phrases, clauses, sentences, paragraphs and sections of this Code. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-46) 
Sec. 1-3-67. - Amendments to Code. 
(a)  All ordinances passed subsequent to this Code of Ordinances, which amend, repeal or in any way affect this Code, may be numbered in accordance with the numbering system of this Code and printed for inclusion herein, or in the case of chapters, sections and subsections or any part thereof repealed by subsequent ordinances, the repealed portions may be excluded from the Code by omission from reprinted pages affected thereby, and the subsequent ordinances as numbered and printed or omitted, in the case of repeal, shall be prima facie evidence of the subsequent ordinances until the time that this Code and subsequent ordinances numbered or omitted are readopted as a new code of ordinances. 
(b)  Amendments to any of the provisions of this Code may be made by specific reference to the section number of this Code in the following language: "That Section ____________ of the Code of Ordinances of the Town of Batesburg-Leesville, South Carolina, is hereby amended to read as follows: ____________ ." The new provisions shall then be set out in full as enacted. 
(c)  In the event a new section not heretofore existing in the Code is to be added, the following language may be used: "That the Code of Ordinances of the Town of Batesburg-Leesville, South Carolina is hereby amended by adding a section, to be numbered ____________ , which section reads as follows: ____________ ." The new section shall then be set out in full as enacted. 
(d)  In lieu of the foregoing subsection, when the town council desires to enact an ordinance of a general and permanent nature embracing a subject not previously existing in the Code, but which the town council desires to incorporate into the Code, a provision in substantially the following language may be made a part of the ordinance: "It is the intention of the town council, and it is hereby ordained, that the provisions of this ordinance shall become and be made part of the Code of Ordinances of the Town of Batesburg-Leesville, South Carolina, and the sections of this ordinance may be renumbered to accomplish that intention." 
(e)  All sections, articles, chapters or provisions desired to be repealed must be specifically repealed by section, article or chapter number, as the case may be. 
(f)  When necessary, sections and subsections to the Code may be renumbered by the official codifier for the town to fulfill the intent of the governing body, but all such changes shall be approved in advance by the town attorney. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-47) 
Sec. 1-3-68. - Altering Code. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to change or amend by additions or deletions, any part or portion of this Code, or to insert or delete pages, or portions thereof, or to alter or tamper with the Code in any manner whatsoever, which will cause the law of the town to be misrepresented thereby. Any person, firm or corporation violating this section shall be punished as provided in section 1-3-69. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-48) 
Sec. 1-3-69. - General penalty. 
(a)  Whenever in this Code or in any ordinance or resolution of the town, or rule, regulation or order promulgated by any officer or agency of the town under authority duly vested in him or it, any act is prohibited or is made or declared to be unlawful or an offense or misdemeanor, or the doing of any act is required, or the failure to do any act is declared to be unlawful or an offense or misdemeanor, and no specific penalty is provided for the violation thereof, the violation of such provisions of this Code, or any such ordinance, resolution, rule, regulation or order shall be punished by a fine not exceeding $500.00 and/or by imprisonment for a period not exceeding 30 days; provided, however, that no penalty shall exceed the penalty provided by state law for similar offenses. 
(b)  Each day any violation of this Code or any such ordinance, rule or regulation shall continue shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-49) 
Sec. 1-3-70. - Liability of corporations and/or agents for violations. 
    Any violation of this Code by any officer, agent or other person acting for or employed by any corporation or unincorporated association or organization while acting within the scope of his office or employment, shall, in every case, also be deemed to be a violation by such corporation, association or organization. The individual shall be subject and liable to punishment as well as such corporation or unincorporated association or organization for the violation by it of any provision of this Code, where such violation was the act or omission, or the result of the act, omission or order of any such person. 
(Code 1996, § 1-3-50) 
Sec. 1-3-71. - Certain ordinances, rights, etc., not affected by Code. 
    Nothing in this Code, or the ordinance adopting this Code, shall affect any of the following ordinances or previous Code's sections in effect at the time of adoption of this Code, until later amended or repealed: 
(1)  Any offense or act committed or done or any penalty or forfeiture incurred or any contract or right established or accruing before the effective date of the ordinance from which this Code is derived; 
(2)  Any ordinance or resolution promising or guaranteeing the payment of money for the town, or authorizing the issuance of any bonds of the town or any evidence of the town's indebtedness, or any contract or obligations assumed by the town; 
(3)  The administrative ordinances or resolutions of the town not in conflict with the provisions of this Code; 
(4)  Any ordinance or resolution fixing salaries of officers or employees of the town, unless superseded; 
(5)  Any appropriation ordinance or resolution, including tax levies and other charges; 
(6)  Any right of franchise granted by the council to any person, firm or corporation; 
(7)  Any ordinance or resolution dedicating, naming, establishing, locating, relocating, closing, opening, paving, widening, vacating, etc., any street or public way in the town; 
(8)  Any ordinance or resolution establishing and prescribing the street grades of any streets in the town; 
(9)  Any ordinance or resolution providing for local improvements, or assessing taxes therefor; 
(10)  Any ordinance or resolution dedicating or accepting any plat or subdivision in the town, or providing regulations for the same; 
(11)  Any ordinance annexing property to the town; 
(12)  Any zoning ordinance, development standards, or amendments thereto; 
(13)  Any ordinance or resolution regulating the erection, alteration, repair, demolition, moving, or removal of buildings or other structures; 
(14)  Ordinances or resolutions prescribing traffic regulations for specific locations, prescribing through streets, parking limitations, parking prohibitions, one-way traffic, limitations on loads of vehicles, or loading zones, not inconsistent with this Code; 
(15)  Any ordinance or resolution fixing utility rates and charges; 
(16)  Any ordinance of agreement with another political subdivision; 
(17)  Any ordinance concerning the issuance of tax anticipation notes or other debt; or 
(18)  Any other ordinance or resolution, or part thereof, which is not of a general and permanent nature, or which is referred to elsewhere in this Code as continuing in effect; 
and all such ordinances and resolutions are hereby recognized as continuing in full force and effect to the same extent as if set out at length in this Code. Such ordinances and resolutions are on file in the clerk's office. 
CHAPTER 4. - OFFICERS AND DEPARTMENTS 

Sec. 1-4-1. - Council's powers. 
    The town council may by ordinance, upon recommendation of the town manager, create, change and abolish offices, departments or agencies of the municipal government in addition to those created by this chapter and may prescribe the functions of all departments, offices and agencies, except that no function assigned by law to a particular department, office or agency may be discontinued or assigned to any other agency. The head of each department shall be designated director thereof and shall have supervision and control over his department subject, however, to the direction of the manager. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-1) 
State Law reference- Authority to establish offices, departments and agencies, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-13-100. 
Sec. 1-4-2. - Creation of specific departments. 
    There are hereby established and created the following departments for the town: 
(1)  Police; 
(2)  Fire; 
(3)  Administration; 
(4)  Sewer and water; 
(5)  Street; 
(6)  Maintenance; 
(7)  Planning/zoning. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-2) 
Sec. 1-4-3. - Town manager-Appointment, salary and term. 
    The town council shall select and appoint a manager whose salary shall be fixed by the council and whose term of office shall be indefinite. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-3) 
State Law reference- Employment of manager, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-13-50; term, compensation, and removal, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-13-70. 
Sec. 1-4-4. - Same-Qualifications. 
    The town manager shall be employed solely on the basis of his executive qualifications. He need not be a resident of the town or state at the time of appointment, and he may reside outside the town while in office with the approval of the council. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-4) 
State Law reference- Qualifications of manager, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-13-50. 
Sec. 1-4-5. - Same-Bond. 
    The town manager shall provide a bond for the faithful performance of his duties in such amount as may be determined by the council, the premium for which shall be paid by the town. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-5) 
State Law reference- Surety bonds of manager, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-13-60. 
Sec. 1-4-6. - Same-Powers and duties. 
(a)  The town manager shall be the chief executive officer of the town and head of the administrative branch of the municipal government. 
(b)  The town manager shall be responsible to the council for the proper administration of all affairs of the municipality and his responsibilities shall include: 
(1)  Appointing (and removing, when necessary) appointive officers and employees of the municipality, and fixing the salaries of such officers and employees, unless otherwise provided by law; provided, that he may authorize heads of departments or offices to appoint and remove subordinates in their respective departments or offices; 
(2)  Preparing the municipality's annual budget, submitting it to the council and administering the budget as adopted; 
(3)  Preparing and submitting to the council a complete annual report on the finances and administrative activities of the town at the end of each fiscal year; 
(4)  Making such other financial reports as may be required by the council from time to time; 
(5)  Keeping the council advised of the financial condition and future needs of the municipality and making such recommendations as he may deem desirable; and 
(6)  Performing such other duties as may be required by law or assigned by the council. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-6) 
State Law reference- Responsibilities of manager, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-13-90. 
Sec. 1-4-7. - Acting town manager. 
(a)  By letter filed with the town clerk-treasurer, the manager shall designate a qualified administrative officer to perform his duties during his temporary absence or disability. 
(b)  In the event of the manager's failure to make such designation, the council may, by resolution, appoint an officer of the municipality to perform the duties of the manager until he shall return, or his disability shall cease. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-7) 
State Law reference- Similar state law, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-13-80. 
Sec. 1-4-8. - Removal of town manager. 
    The town council may remove the town manager at any time upon giving him written notification of the reasons for the proposed removal and the right to a public hearing before council. Within five days after such notice is delivered to the manager, he may file with the council a written request for a public hearing, such hearing to be held not less than 20, nor more than 30, days after the request is filed. The manager may file with the council a written reply no later than five days before the hearing. Removal shall be stayed pending the decision at the public hearing. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-8) 
State Law reference- Removal of town manager, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-13-70. 
Sec. 1-4-9. - Town clerk-treasurer-Term. 
    The town manager shall appoint a clerk-treasurer for the municipality who shall hold office for a term of two years. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-9) 
State Law reference- Appointment of municipal clerk, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-220. 
Sec. 1-4-10. - Same-Bond. 
    Before entering upon the duties of his office, the clerk-treasurer shall enter into a bond, in such sum as may be required and with such surety company as shall be approved by the council, for the faithful performance of his duties. 
(Code 1978, § 2-71; Code 1996, § 1-4-10) 
State Law reference- Surety bonds of municipal employees, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-13-60. 
Sec. 1-4-11. - Same-Duties. 
    The clerk-treasurer shall: 
(1)  Attend all meetings of the council and keep all records of the proceedings of the council in a book that shall be kept for that purpose; 
(2)  Give notice of council meetings to its members and the public; 
(3)  Collect and record all taxes and fees due the town and keep a record of all moneys belonging to the town and pay out same upon proper authority of the council; 
(4)  Submit to council a monthly statement of the financial condition of the town showing the balance on hand at the commencement of the month, all receipts and disbursements during the month, and the current balance; and 
(5)  Perform such other duties as assigned. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-11) 
State Law reference- Duties of municipal clerk, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-220. 
Sec. 1-4-12. - Town attorney. 
    At its first regular meeting after a general election, the town council shall elect a lawyer, who has had at least two years' experience at the bar, as the town attorney. The attorney shall hold office for two years or until his successor is elected and qualified and shall receive such compensation as shall be fixed by council. The town attorney shall not be considered an officer of the municipality. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-12) 
State Law reference- Municipal attorney, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-230. 
Sec. 1-4-13. - Enforcement of ordinances, laws, etc. 
    All officers and employees of the town shall enforce obedience to such statutes, provisions of this Code or any other ordinances, resolutions, regulations, or orders issued thereunder, as may relate to their regular duties, or with whose enforcement they are properly chargeable, by properly reporting any violation thereof and instituting such proceedings as may be necessary to such enforcement. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-13) 
Sec. 1-4-14. - Right of entry. 
    Whenever any officer or employee of the town is required or authorized by statute, the provisions of this Code, or any thereunder to enter any premises or vehicle, he shall have the right to enter the premises or vehicle at any reasonable time in pursuance of such duties, except as prohibited by the Constitution or laws of this state or of the United States. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-14) 
Sec. 1-4-15. - Resisting or interfering with officers or employees. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to resist or interfere with any member of the police department, any member of the fire department, or any other municipal officer or employee in the discharge of his lawful duties. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-15) 
Sec. 1-4-16. - Municipal officers may not contract with town; exception. 
    No municipal officer shall take a contract to perform work or furnish material for the town, and no officer shall receive any compensation on any such contract, except any municipal officer may enter into a contract awarded to him as low bidder after a public call for bids and which is allowed by unanimous vote of the town council upon each particular contract, such vote to be taken by yeas and nays and entered upon the council's minutes. 
(Code 1996, § 1-4-16) 
State Law reference- Municipal officers prohibited from contracting with municipality, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-21-30; conflict of interest, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-130. 
CHAPTER 5. - FINANCIAL ADMINISTRATION 
ARTICLE A. - GENERAL PROVISIONS[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Council to provide for annual independent audits, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-240; adoption of annual budget and tax levy, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-11-40; collection of delinquent ad valorem property taxes by municipalities, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-300; local fee imposition limitations, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-1-330; towns over 200 population must publish financial statements, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-21-50; Municipal Bond Act, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-21-210 et seq.; bonded indebtedness of political subdivisions, S.C. Const. art. X, § 14. 

Sec. 1-5-1. - Fiscal year. 
    The fiscal year of the town shall be July 1 to June 30 of each year. 
(Code 1996, § 1-5-1) 
Sec. 1-5-2. - Adoption of budget. 
    The prepared budget and the estimated revenue for payment of budgeted expenses are hereby adopted by reference and are made a part of this Code as fully as if incorporated herein. 
(Code 1996, § 1-5-2) 
Sec. 1-5-3. - Form of budget; transfers of appropriations; lapse of appropriations. 
(a)  The annual budget shall take the form of an appropriation ordinance, setting out the estimated revenues in detail by source and making appropriations according to fund and by organizational unit, purpose or activity as set out in the budget document. The amounts thus set out in the adopted operating budget for each organizational unit, purpose or activity shall then constitute the annual appropriation for such item and no expenditure shall be made or encumbrance created in excess of the otherwise unencumbered balance of the appropriation to which it is chargeable. No interdepartmental transfers of the appropriations from one line item account to another line item account in the operating funds of the town shall be made, unless upon approval by majority vote of the total membership of the town council. This approval shall be in the form of an amendment to the annual operating budget ordinance. 
(b)  The council shall adopt the final capital improvements budget for the ensuing fiscal year in the form of an ordinance. No appropriations provided for in the capital improvements budget shall lapse until the purpose for which the appropriation was made shall have been accomplished or abandoned. Provided, however, any member of the council may submit amendments to the capital improvements budget at any time during the fiscal year, which amendments may be accompanied by recommendations thereon by the town manager or the town planner. Any amendments to the capital improvements budget ordinance shall become effective only upon adoption by a majority of the total members of the council. 
(c)  Following adoption by ordinance of the annual operating and capital improvements budget for each fiscal year, the council shall levy by ordinance a tax upon all real and personal property within the city. The rates to be set by the ordinance shall be such that a reasonable estimate of cash revenues of the levy shall be at least sufficient, together with other anticipated revenues, fund balances and applicable reserves to equal the total amount appropriated for each of the several funds set forth in the annual operating budget ordinance for defraying the expense of the city. 
(d)  Upon a certification of the clerk-treasurer that the revenues or any other resources actually realized with respect to any fund shall be less than was anticipated and will be insufficient to meet the amounts appropriated from the funds, it shall be the duty of the council to impound any appropriations as may be necessary to prevent a deficit operation. 
(e)  The town council may make appropriations in addition to those contained in the current operation budget and capital improvements budget ordinance at any regular or special meeting called for such purpose. 
(f)  All unencumbered balances of appropriations in the current operating budget at the end of the fiscal year shall lapse into the general fund of the town and be expended as the council may direct. 
(Code 1996, § 1-5-3) 
Sec. 1-5-4. - Annual property tax. 
    The council shall impose by ordinance, a copy of which shall be published at least ten days before the adoption thereof and setting forth the amounts levied for the several purposes for which levies may be made, an annual tax on all real estate lying within the corporate limits and on all personal property within the corporate limits and on all personal property within the town, including bonds and stocks of banks, insurance companies and other corporations and the real estate of churches and school associations from which the church and school associations draw a revenue or which is intended to be rented out for that purpose, except property that is exempt from taxation under the constitution and laws of this state, as will yield an amount necessary for the general fund operating purposes and for debt service requirements of the town. A change in the tax shall be by ordinance and in accordance with the above notice requirement for such. 
(Code 1978, § 21-1; Code 1996, § 1-5-4) 
Sec. 1-5-5. - Town credit card. 
(a)  The town council and mayor have decided that it is appropriate to have a town credit card through a local bank. 
(b)  The authorized signatories on said credit card shall be the town manager and the mayor. 
(c)  The town shall secure a credit card from and through a local bank for use of town purposes with the persons authorized to sign for charges made to said credit card being the town manager and the mayor. 
(Code 1996, § 1-5-5) 
Secs. 1-5-6-1-5-10. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE B. - COLLECTION OF PROPERTY TAX[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Editor's note- Pursuant to authority provided by state law, municipal property taxes are collected by Lexington County. 
State Law reference- Collection of delinquent ad valorem taxes by municipalities, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-300. 

Sec. 1-5-11. - Basis of assessment. 
    The annual property tax shall be levied on property within the corporate limits as assessed for taxation for state and county purposes, adopting as a basis for such assessment the return and assessment for the current year in the office of the county auditor and treasurer for the county for the purpose of levying state and county taxes for the current year. 
(Code 1996, § 1-5-11) 
State Law reference- Municipal authorities may copy assessment from county books, S.C. Code 1976, § 12-37-40. 
Sec. 1-5-12. - Due date of taxes. 
    All taxes, except those on motor vehicles, shall be due and payable between October 1 and January 15 (of the following year) after assessment in each year. 
(Code 1996, § 1-5-12) 
State Law reference- Municipal taxes on motor vehicles, S.C. Code 1976, § 12-37-2690. 
Sec. 1-5-13. - Penalties. 
    There shall be added to all delinquent taxes the following penalties: 
(1)  Three percent of the tax if paid between January 16 to February 1; 
(2)  Ten percent if paid between February 2 to March 16; and 
(3)  15 percent plus a $15.00 execution charge if paid on March 17 or later. 
(Code 1976, § 21-21; Code 1996, § 1-5-13) 
CHAPTER 6. - MUNICIPAL COURT[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
Editor's note- The municipal court may (1) Under S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-6150, try and determine criminal cases involving violations of S.C. Code 1976, Title 56, Chapter 5, occurring within the respective limits of this municipality, when the penalty prescribed by Title 56, Chapter 5 for such violations does not exceed 30 days' imprisonment nor a $100.00 fine, and may have trial jurisdiction over such criminal cases the same as magistrates; (2) Under S.C. Code 1976, § 61-6-4500, try and determine all cases involving a violation of S.C. Code 1976, § 61-6-13, except § 61-6-4720, per § 61-6-4500; (3) Maintain jurisdiction for trial of persons under 17 years of age, for alleged violations of S.C. Code 1976, Title 50, when the court would have jurisdiction if the offense charged was committed by an adult; and (4) Try a first offense for violation of S.C. Code 1976, § 47-1-40 (ill-treatment of animals). 
State Law reference- Municipal courts, S.C. Code 1976, § 14-25-5 et seq.; powers, duties and jurisdiction of municipal court, S.C. Code 1976, § 14-25-45; trial jurisdiction of municipal courts for violations of Uniform Act Regulating Traffic, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-6150; trial of persons charged with violations of ordinances or state law, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-90; municipal judges generally, S.C. Code 1976, § 14-25-15; appointment and duties of clerk of court, S.C. Code 1976, § 14-25-35; appointment, duties and powers of ministerial recorder, S.C. Code 1976, § 14-25-115; maximum penalties imposed by municipal court, S.C. Code 1976, § 14-25-65; judge may suspend sentences, S.C. Code 1976, § 14-25-75; disposition of fines and penalties, S.C. Code 1976, § 14-25-85; appeals to Court of Common Pleas, S.C. Code 1976, § 14-25-95; municipal judge to make return, S.C. Code 1976, § 14-25-105; jury commissioners, S.C. Code 1976, § 14-25-135; demand for jury trial; composition, S.C. Code 1976, § 14-25-125. 

Sec. 1-6-1. - Creation. 
    There is hereby established a municipal court for the town, which shall be a part of the unified judicial system of the state, pursuant to Action No. 480 of 1980, for the trial and determination of all cases within its jurisdiction. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-1) 
Sec. 1-6-2. - Jurisdiction. 
    The municipal court shall have jurisdiction to try all cases arising under the ordinances of the town. The court shall also have all such powers, duties and jurisdiction in criminal cases made under state law and conferred upon magistrates. The court shall have the power to punish for contempt of court by imposition of sentences up to the limits imposed on municipal courts. The court shall have no jurisdiction in civil matters. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-2) 
Sec. 1-6-3. - Judge-Term; compensation. 
    The court shall be presided over by the municipal judge, who shall be appointed by the council for a term of two years, and until his successor is appointed and qualified. The compensation of the municipal judge shall be determined by the council from time to time. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-3) 
Sec. 1-6-4. - Same-Powers and duties. 
    The municipal judge shall have such powers and duties as provided by the Constitution and Code of Laws of South Carolina and such other duties, not inconsistent therewith, as may be ordained by the town council. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-4) 
Sec. 1-6-5. - Clerk. 
    The council shall designate a clerk of the municipal court who shall keep such records and make such reports as may be required by the municipal judge or the state court administrator. The council may designate the municipal clerk-treasurer or any other municipal employee to serve as clerk of the court. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-5) 
Sec. 1-6-6. - Disposition of fines and penalties. 
    All fines and penalties collected by the municipal court shall be turned over to the municipal clerk-treasurer for deposit to the general fund of the town. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-6) 
Sec. 1-6-7. - Penalties imposed. 
    Whenever the municipal judge or a jury finds a party guilty of violating a municipal ordinance or the state law within the jurisdiction of the court, he may impose a fine or imprisonment or both, not to exceed $500.00 or 30 days. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-7) 
Sec. 1-6-8. - Suspend sentence. 
    The municipal judge may suspend sentences imposed by him upon such terms and conditions as he deems proper including, without limitation, restitution or public service employment. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-8) 
Sec. 1-6-9. - Notice of appeal. 
    Any party shall have the right to appeal from the sentence or judgment of the municipal court to the Court of Common Pleas. Notice of intention to appeal, setting forth the grounds for appeal, shall be given in writing and served on the municipal judge or the clerk of the municipal court within ten days after sentence is passed or judgment rendered, or the appeal shall be deemed waived. The party appealing shall enter into a bond, payable to the town to appear and defend such appeal at the next term of the Court of Common Pleas or shall pay the fine assessed. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-9) 
Sec. 1-6-10. - Appeal. 
    In the event of an appeal, the municipal judge shall make a return to the Court of Common Pleas as provided by S.C. Code 1976, § 14-25-95. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-10) 
Sec. 1-6-11. - Jury trial. 
    Any person to be tried in the municipal court may, prior to trial, demand, in writing, a jury trial, and such jury, when demanded, shall be composed of six persons prescribed by law. The right to a jury trial shall be deemed to have been waived unless a written demand is made prior to trial. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-11) 
Sec. 1-6-12. - Ministerial recorder. 
    There is hereby established the office of ministerial recorder. Ministerial recorders shall be elected from time to time by council, and shall serve at its pleasure or until the office is vacated when employment with the municipality is terminated. Ministerial recorders shall perform the powers provided by law, and shall be subject to the supervision of the municipal judge. Ministerial recorders shall not be law enforcement officers. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-12) 
Sec. 1-6-13. - Contempt of court. 
    Any person failing to maintain proper decorum, or failing to have the proper attire or refusing to obey the orders of the recorder, while acting in his official capacity, shall be guilty of contempt of court. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-13) 
Sec. 1-6-14. - Failure to obey a subpoena or summons. 
    Any person that is summoned or subpoenaed to appear in recorder's court shall do so unless he has a just and legal excuse. If any person fails to appear, he shall be guilty of contempt of court and shall be punished by a fine not exceeding $500.00 or imprisonment for not more than 30 days. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-14) 
Sec. 1-6-15. - Prosecution in magistrate's courts. 
    The town, pursuant to the authority of Act No. 480 of 1980, may prosecute all of its cases arising under the ordinances of the town or traffic laws of this state in the magistrate's courts of Lexington County or Saluda County. Such courts are hereby vested with the authority to try and determine all cases arising under municipal ordinance or state law within the jurisdiction of municipal or magistrate's courts. 
(Code 1996, § 1-6-15) 
CHAPTER 7. - ELECTIONS[6] 

Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
State Law reference- Nominations and elections for municipal offices, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-15-20 et seq. 

Sec. 1-7-1. - Election at large. 
(a)  The mayor shall be elected by the town at large. 
(b)  The members of council shall be elected by districts. 
(Code 1996, § 1-7-1) 
Sec. 1-7-2. - Districts. 
    The town shall be divided into eight election districts, the boundaries of which shall be as shown on an official map duly adopted by the town council on file in the office of the town clerk-treasurer and incorporated herein by reference. 
(Code 1996, § 1-7-2) 
Sec. 1-7-3. - Method of election. 
(a)  All regular and special elections for the offices of mayor and town council shall be nonpartisan, using the election and runoff method pursuant to S.C. Code 1976, § 5-15-62. 
(b)  Nomination petitions for the offices of mayor shall be filed with the Municipal clerk-treasurer at least 45 days prior to the date of the election concerned and shall bear the signatures of not less than five percent of the qualified voters. They shall be delivered by the clerk-treasurer for examination, its validity determined not later than 30 days prior to the election. 
(c)  Nomination petitions for the offices of council members shall be filed with the municipal clerk-treasurer at least 45 days prior to the date of the election concerned and shall bear the signatures of not less than the five percent of the qualified electors of the district. The municipal clerk-treasurer shall deliver the petition for examination of the petition and determine its validity not later than 30 days prior to the election. 
(d)  No political party affiliation shall be placed on any ballots for any candidate. 
(Code 1996, § 1-7-3) 
Sec. 1-7-4. - When held. 
(a)  All general elections to fill the offices of mayor and council members shall be held on the first Tuesday following the first Monday in November of each odd-numbered year. 
(b)  In case a vacancy shall occur in the office of mayor or any of the council members, an election shall be held to fill such vacancy; provided that the vacancy occurs 180 days or more prior to the next general election. 
(Code 1996, § 1-7-4) 
State Law reference- Filling vacancies, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-200. 
Sec. 1-7-5. - Notice of elections. 
    At least 60 days public notice of every general or special election shall be given by publication thereof in a newspaper of general circulation in the town. 
(Code 1996, § 1-7-5) 
State Law reference- Public notice of election, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-15-50. 
Sec. 1-7-6. - Where held. 
    All elections shall be at such places in the town as shall be designated by the town council in accordance with the state law. 
(Code 1996, § 1-7-6) 
Sec. 1-7-7. - Transfer of authority for conducting municipal elections to the Lexington County Registration and Election Commission. 
(a)  The Lexington County Voter Registration and Elections Commission shall advertise municipal elections, prepare and distribute ballots and election materials, appoint managers of election for each polling place, and otherwise supervise and conduct all municipal elections within the town. 
(b)  Immediately upon the closing of the polls at any municipal election in the town, the Lexington County Voter Registration and Elections Commission shall begin to count and continuously count the votes cast and make a statement of the whole number of votes cast in such election together with the number of votes cast for each candidate for mayor and councilperson, canvass the vote and publicly display the unofficial results. 
(c)  The voter registration and elections commission shall thereafter certify the results of the elections and transmit the certified results to the town council or an appointed authority representing the town government as soon as practicable following the certification. 
(d)  Accept candidate filings, and filing fees/petitions, including, but not limited to, notices of candidacy, candidacy pledges, hear and decide protests and certify the results of municipal elections. 
(e)  Utilize an automated election system and computer counting with the count publicly conducted. 
(f)  The town election commission is hereby dissolved. 
(Code 1996, § 1-7-7; Ord. of 10-12-2015) 
State Law reference- Home Rule Act of 1975, S.C. Code 1976, §§ 5-7-30, 5-7-260, 5-15-145. 
Title 2 - PUBLIC SAFETY 
CHAPTER 1. - LAW ENFORCEMENT[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal police officers, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-110. 

Sec. 2-1-1. - Composition of department. 
    The police department shall consist of one chief and such other police officers as from time to time the town council shall deem necessary for the safety and good order of the town. 
(Code 1996, § 2-1-1) 
Sec. 2-1-2. - Appointment. 
(a)  The chief of police shall be appointed by the town manager. 
(b)  The other police officers shall be appointed by the town manager upon recommendation of the chief. 
(c)  In case of an emergency, the town manager may appoint as many special police officers as he deems necessary. Special officers shall be administered an oath of office by the mayor. 
(Code 1996, § 2-1-2) 
Sec. 2-1-3. - Terms. 
    Each police officer shall serve and continue to serve for so long a period as he shall perform his duties and does not violate any rule, regulation or policy of the department or of the town. Special police shall serve as such only for the period stated in their appointment. 
(Code 1996, § 2-1-3) 
Sec. 2-1-4. - Compensation. 
    The compensation of all police officers, including the chief of police shall be determined by the town manager. 
(Code 1996, § 2-1-4) 
Sec. 2-1-5. - Swearing in and empowering. 
    Each member of the department shall be sworn in and thereupon vested with all the powers of constables within the corporate limits of the town or its police jurisdiction, and shall also have the power to carry out all duties assigned to him by statute, ordinance, resolution, directive, rule, or regulation as is necessary, specifically or by implication. 
(Code 1996, § 2-1-5) 
Sec. 2-1-6. - Bond required. 
    The chief of police shall be required to enter into bond, in such sum as shall be set by council from time to time for the faithful performance of his duties and his personnel. 
(Code 1996, § 2-1-6) 
Sec. 2-1-7. - Policies, rules and procedures. 
(a)  The council, with the advice of the chief of police and the town manager, shall prescribe policies, rules and regulations for the department. 
(b)  A compilation of all policies, rules and regulations, plus a list of the shift and officers in charge shall be made by the chief of police and posted in a conspicuous place within the police department. This list shall be kept current. 
(Code 1996, § 2-1-7) 
Sec. 2-1-9. - Obedience to chief. 
    The chief of police at all times shall be recognized and respected by each member of the department as his commander and superior officer. All disregard, inattention or disobedience of the proper general or special orders of the chief shall be reported to him. 
(Code 1996, § 2-1-9) 
Sec. 2-1-10. - Supervision by chief. 
    It shall be the duty of the chief of police to distribute the members of his department over the town to obtain the best results and most efficient service. He shall initiate such programs as will provide him with information and reports and shall maintain regular contact with members of the department. 
(Code 1996, § 2-1-10) 
Sec. 2-1-11. - Duties of police. 
(a)  It shall be the duty of each police officer to arrest and/or report any person for violating in any manner the laws of ordinances of the town and failure or neglect to do so shall make him liable to fine, suspension or discharge. 
(b)  All members of the police department must be made aware of the fact that they are the representatives to the public at large of the town and that their actions and appearances must at all times reflect credit on the town. 
(c)  A copy of this chapter, together with all current rules, regulations and policies, shall be read to each new member of the police department at the time he is sworn in and shall also be read to all members of the police department once each year by the chief of police. 
(Code 1996, § 2-1-11) 
Sec. 2-1-12. - Resisting, interfering with officer in execution of warrant; other process. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to resist, assault, obstruct, hinder, prevent or in any manner interfere with any officer or other person charged with the execution of any lawful warrant or other process in arresting any person for whose apprehension the warrant has been issued; or to rescue or attempt to rescue any person from the custody of an officer or person lawfully arresting him; or directly or indirectly to aid, abet or assist any person so arrested to escape from custody; or to harbor or conceal any person for whose arrest a warrant or other process shall have been issued, so as to prevent the discovery of the person, after notice or knowledge of the fact of the issuing of the warrant or other process. It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully approach nearer than 20 feet to any police officer who is making or attempting to make an arrest or while on his way to jail with his prisoner. All police officers shall have the right to order all persons away from the vicinity of the jail while any person is being placed therein or being held in custody. Any person violating any part of this section or refusing to leave the vicinity of the jail when ordered to do so by a police officer shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1996, § 2-1-12) 
Sec. 2-1-13. - Municipal court powers and duties. 
    The chief of police or his designee shall attend all sessions of the municipal court. The chief of police and police officers shall be subject to the orders of the court and shall execute the orders, writs and mandates thereof, and perform such other duties in connection with the court as may be prescribed by ordinance.
