CHAPTER 3. - ADVERTISING 

Sec. 7-3-1. - Posting on public property-Prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful to place any advertisement, business, political or otherwise, or any notice or sign of any nature on public property within the town, by the use of a placard, picture, paper, circular, painting, or by any means or device whatsoever. 
(Code 1996, § 7-3-1) 
Sec. 7-3-2. - Same-Property in which town has interest. 
    It shall be unlawful to place any advertisement, notice or sign of any nature on property in which the town has an interest or the right to regulate, including, but not limited to, telephone and telegraph poles, and electric poles and towers. 
(Code 1996, § 7-3-2) 
Sec. 7-3-3. - Posting on private property. 
    It shall be unlawful to place any advertisement, notice or sign of any nature on private property within the town, without written consent of the owner or lessee of the property. 
(Code 1996, § 7-3-3) 
Sec. 7-3-4. - Penalties. 
    Any violation of the provisions of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1996, § 7-3-4) 
CHAPTER 4. - YARD SALES 

Sec. 7-4-1. - Permit required; definition. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to conduct a yard sale within the town limits, unless such person shall first obtain a permit from the town clerk-treasurer. The cost of such permit shall be as fixed by the council from time to time; provided that persons age 62 and over are exempt from payment of the permit fee. 
(b)  For the purposes of this chapter, the term "yard sale" is defined as the sale or trading of clothing, furniture, household items, food, dishes, antiques or similar goods or merchandise, other than in the normal course of business, or the sale or trading of such goods, as outlined above, by a person not regularly engaged in such business. Such goods or merchandise do not need to be attended for a sale to be deemed to be in existence. The term "yard sale" shall include garage sales, attic or carport sales and similar types of sales or events. 
(Code 1996, § 7-4-1) 
Sec. 7-4-2. - Where held. 
    Yard sales shall be held only on property owned, leased or rented for residential purposes by the person applying for the permit. 
(Code 1996, § 7-4-2) 
Sec. 7-4-3. - Owner of property liable. 
    It shall be unlawful for the owner of any property within the town to knowingly permit any person to hold or conduct a yard sale on such property: 
(1)  Without having first secured a permit therefor in accordance with this chapter; or 
(2)  If the property is not used for residential purposes. 
(Code 1996, § 7-4-3) 
Sec. 7-4-4. - Permit requirements. 
(a)  At least 24 hours prior to conducting a yard sale, a permit for the yard sale shall be secured from the town clerk-treasurer. Upon application for a permit, an applicant shall be given the opportunity to review the provisions of this chapter. 
(b)  Information presented by the applicant for a yard sale permit shall include the following: 
(1)  The name and address of the person conducting, operating, sponsoring, and/or promoting a sale regulated herein; 
(2)  Location at which the sale is to be conducted; 
(3)  The date on which the sale is to be conducted; and 
(4)  The time period of the day during which it is proposed to carry on the sale. 
(c)  If information submitted by the applicant indicates that the proposed yard sale activity will be in compliance with the provisions of this chapter, a permit for the yard sale shall be issued by the town. If it is determined by the clerk-treasurer that a permit should not be issued, that termination shall be appealable to the town council. All permits shall be displayed at the location of the sale in a conspicuous manner. Each permit shall be valid only for time and place specified in the application. The term "person" herein shall be taken to mean individuals, firms, corporations, partnerships, clubs, associations or any other such groups. 
(Code 1996, § 7-4-4) 
Sec. 7-4-5. - Maximum period and number of permits. 
    The maximum period for each yard or garage sale permit shall be two days consecutively. The maximum number of permits allowed is three per family, per location, per calendar year. All signs shall be removed 24 hours after the sale. 
(Code 1996, § 7-4-5) 
Sec. 7-4-6. - Penalty. 
    Any person violating the provisions of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1996, § 7-4-6) 
CHAPTER 5. - ASSEMBLIES, PARADES AND PROCESSIONS 

Sec. 7-5-1. - Enforcement. 
    Nothing contained in this chapter shall prohibit the authority of any officer to arrest a person engaged in any act or activity granted a permit under this chapter, if the conduct of such person violates the laws of the state, provisions of this Code or other ordinances of the town, or unreasonably obstructs the public streets and sidewalks of the town, or engages in acts that cause, or would tend to cause, a breach of the peace. 
(Code 1996, § 7-5-1) 
Sec. 7-5-2. - Permit required. 
    It shall be unlawful for any group of ten or more persons to organize or hold or participate in any parade, meeting, assembly or procession of persons and/or vehicles on the streets or sidewalks of the town, unless such activity shall have first been authorized by a written permit therefor. 
(Code 1996, § 7-5-2) 
Sec. 7-5-3. - Application for permit. 
    Any person desiring a permit required by the provisions of this chapter shall make application therefor to the town manager, which application shall contain the following information: 
(1)  The name and address of the applicant; 
(2)  The name and address of the person the applicant represents; 
(3)  The exact time and date of commencement and termination of each act or activity desired; 
(4)  The purpose, location and route of such act or activity, if applicable; 
(5)  The person, group, association or body to be authorized under the permit to do such act or activity and the number of persons to participate; and 
(6)  Such other relevant information as the town manager may require for the investigation of the applicant. 
(Code 1996, § 7-5-3) 
Sec. 7-5-4. - Contents of permit. 
    Upon issuance of a permit required by this chapter, the same shall contain therein all information contained in the application therefor and be signed by the town manager and a signed copy of the same shall be kept with application, both on file in the office of the town manager. 
(Code 1996, § 7-5-4) 
Sec. 7-5-5. - Matters considered in determining issuance of permit. 
    In deciding whether to issue a permit under the provisions of this chapter, the town manager shall consider: 
(1)  The number of persons to participate; 
(2)  The anticipated traffic conditions at the time and date proposed for the activity; 
(3)  The schedule of other similar activities for which permits may have been issued; 
(4)  The adequacy of adult supervision for any minor scheduled to participate; 
(5)  The availability of town personnel whose presence on duty may be required by the activity and by the necessity to protect the general public; and 
(6)  The adequacy of public facilities in the location proposed for the activity to accommodate the proposed activity and the normal public use of public facilities in the proposed location. 
(Code 1996, § 7-5-5) 
Sec. 7-5-6. - Issuance. 
    The permit required by the provisions for this chapter shall be issued by the town manager upon application therefor; provided, however, such permit may be denied or refused if it shall appear that the applicant therefor or the act or activity requested by such application shall be violative of any applicable provision of this Code, state law or other town ordinance. 
(Code 1996, § 7-5-6) 
Sec. 7-5-7. - Deviation from permit. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person participating in any act or activity for which a permit has been granted under the provisions of this chapter to deviate from or alter any of the terms or contents of such permit. 
(Code 1996, § 7-5-7) 
Sec. 7-5-8. - Display of permit. 
    Every person having a permit issued under the provisions of this chapter shall have the permit in his possession during the activity permitted thereby and shall display such permit upon the request of any law enforcement officer. Failure to display such permit shall be deemed a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1996, § 7-5-8) 
Sec. 7-5-9. - Parade fee. 
(a)  Within the town, a parade fee as established by council is to be paid at the time of application to help defray the additional costs of the town to provide security services for any parade conducted within the town which does not fall within one of the two categories below: 
(1)  The parade is put on by any organization whose principle office and base of operations is the town; or 
(2)  Not less than 20 percent of the participants in the parade are citizens and residents of the town. 
(b)  This chapter is cumulative to all other parade ordinances and is not intended to change in any other way the requirements of the town's ordinances as they relate to obtaining parade permits or the conduct of parades within the town. 
(Code 1996, § 7-5-9) 
Sec. 7-5-10. - Carnivals and street shows. 
    All carnivals or street shows by whatever name known are hereby forbidden to show, parade, or otherwise engage in business in the corporate limits of the town unless a business license has been obtained. 
(Code 1996, § 9-1-3) 
State Law reference- Circuses, carnivals, etc., S.C. Code 1976, § 52-1-10 et seq. 
CHAPTER 6. - PAWNBROKER, JUNK AND SECONDHAND DEALERS 

Sec. 7-6-1. - Regulations and requirements. 
(a)  Adoption of state law . All the provisions and requirements of the general laws of the state in regard to pawnbrokers, junk or secondhand dealers and peddlers etc., as covered in S.C. Code 1976, §§ 40-39-10 through 40-39-130 and 40-27-10 through 40-27-40, as amended, insofar as such provisions and amendments have application within the town, are hereby adopted and made a part of this chapter as fully as though set out herein. It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to fail or refuse to comply with the sections of the state law referred to in this subsection or the town ordinance contained in this chapter. 
(b)  Records to be kept . Every person licensed under the provisions of this chapter shall keep a book in which shall be written, at the time of every purchase, barter, pledge, loan or any transactions at his place of business, the name, residence, date of birth, social security number and/or drivers license number of the person from whom an article transacted by him and the hour and date of transaction. All records kept by any person licensed under the provisions of this article shall at all times be subject to the inspection of his records of transactions by the chief of police or any person duly authorized by him, to inspect the same. 
(c)  Report of transactions . Every person licensed under the provisions of this chapter shall make a report to the chief of police by 11:00 a.m. every day, Sunday excepted, concerning all transactions made by him/her since his/her last report. 
(d)  Dealing with minors . No keeper of any pawnshop, pawnbroker, junk shop or secondhand dealer, shall himself, or through any person, either directly or indirectly, purchase or receive, or transact any of the articles mentioned in this article, from any minor or apprentice, without the written permission of the parent, guardian or master of any such minor or apprentice, which written permission shall be filed, and produced whenever required by any person authorized to inspect such shops. 
(e)  Sign required . Every person who shall obtain a pawnbrokers, junk and secondhand dealer license shall put on or over the principal entrance to his shop a sign designating that he is licensed and containing his name. 
(f)  Retention of material . Every article purchased by a licensed pawnshop, pawnbroker, junk shop or secondhand dealer shall be retained in stock by such dealer subject to inspection for at least 48 hours after the purchase thereof. 
(g)  Suspension. revocation of license or pawnshop, pawnbroker, junk and secondhand dealers . Any license issued to pawnshop, pawnbrokers, junk and secondhand dealers may be suspended or revoked by the town council for the violation by the licensee of any applicable provision of this Code, state law or town ordinance, rule or regulation. 
(h)  Junk and secondhand dealer defined . This title as stated in this chapter is taken in the same context as a pawnbroker as defined in S.C. Code 1976, § 40-39-10. 
(Code 1996, § 9-1-21) 
Title 8 - MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Uniform Act Regulating Traffic on Highways, local authority, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-30; powers of local authorities concerning traffic laws, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-710; local traffic control devices, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-930. 

CHAPTER 1. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 8-1-1. - Adoption of state law. 
    There is hereby adopted by reference and made a part hereof as if set out in full those provisions of state law known as the Uniform Act Regulating Traffic on Highways as contained in S.C. Code, Title 56, Chapter 5. 
(Code 1996, § 8-1-1) 
State Law reference- Municipal court's authority to try violations of state traffic laws, S.C. Code 1976, §§ 56-5-6150, 5-7-90. 
Sec. 8-1-2. - Driver's license required. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to operate any motor vehicle upon the streets of the town who does not have a currently valid driver's license. 
(Code 1996, § 8-1-2) 
State Law reference- State license required, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-1-20. 
Sec. 8-1-3. - Powers and duties of council. 
    Except as otherwise directed by this chapter, the town council shall have the power, and is hereby authorized: 
(1)  To regulate the operation and parking of vehicles within the corporate limits of the town by the erection or placing of proper signs or markers indicating prohibition or limited parking, restricted speed areas, one-way streets, play streets, through or arterial streets, parking meter spaces in parking meter zones, U-turns, school zones, hospital zones, loading and unloading zones, quiet zones and other signs, markers and official traffic-control devices indicating the place or manner of operating or parking vehicles within the town; 
(2)  To regulate the movement of pedestrians upon the streets and sidewalks of the town by the erection or placing of proper signs or markers indicating the flow of pedestrian traffic; 
(3)  To designate bus stops and taxicab stands and to erect signs prohibiting the parking of vehicles other than buses and taxicabs at their respective stops and stands; 
(4)  To mark off traffic lanes on streets and parts of streets indicating and directing the flow of traffic, as the council deems necessary; and 
(5)  To secure all necessary signs, markers or official traffic-control devices to be erected or placed on any street or part of a street when such action is deemed necessary. The existence of such signs, markers or official traffic-control devices at any place within the town shall be prima facie evidence that such signs, markers or official traffic-control devices were erected or placed by and at the direction of the council and in accordance with the provisions of this section. 
(Code 1996, § 8-1-3) 
Sec. 8-1-4. - Cleaning glass, etc., from streets. 
(a)  Any person who drops, or permits to be dropped or thrown, upon any street any destructive or injurious material shall immediately remove such material or cause it to be removed. 
(b)  Any person removing a wrecked or damaged vehicle from a street shall remove any glass or other injurious substance dropped upon the street from such vehicle. 
(Code 1996, § 8-1-4) 
Sec. 8-1-5. - Reserved. 
Sec. 8-1-6. - Disposition of fines and forfeitures. 
(a)  All fines or forfeitures collected upon conviction or upon the forfeiture of bail of any person charged with a violation of any of the provisions of this chapter shall be paid into the town treasury and deposited in the general fund of the town. 
(b)  Failure, refusal or neglect on the part of any judicial or other officer or employee receiving or having custody of any such fine or forfeiture to comply with the foregoing provisions of this section shall constitute misconduct in office and shall be grounds for removal therefrom. 
(Code 1996, § 8-1-6) 
Sec. 8-1-7. - Operation prohibited when personal property taxes delinquent. 
    No motor vehicle may be operated upon the public streets or ways or within the corporate limits of the town when the property taxes on such vehicle due the town are delinquent. Personal property taxes assessed against any motor vehicle owned by any citizen of the town shall be delinquent when the same are past due and unpaid and have gone into execution as provided in this Code. 
(Code 1996, § 8-1-7) 
Sec. 8-1-8. - Reports of accidents-Driver. 
    The driver of a vehicle involved in an accident resulting in injury or death of any person or total property damage to an apparent extent of $50.00 or more shall, within 24 hours after such accident, forward a written report of such accident to the police department of the town. 
(Code 1996, § 8-1-8) 
State Law reference- Reports required, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-1260 et seq.; municipalities may require reports, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-1360. 
Sec. 8-1-9. - Same-Duty of occupant. 
    Whenever the driver of a vehicle is physically incapable of making a required accident report and there was another occupant in the vehicle at the time of the accident capable of making a report, such occupant shall make, or cause to be made, such report. 
(Code 1996, § 8-1-9) 
Sec. 8-1-10. - Same-Confidential. 
    All required accident reports and supplemental reports shall be without prejudice to the individual so reporting and shall be for the confidential use of the police department, except that the department may disclose the identity of a person involved in an accident when such identity is not otherwise known or when such person denies his presence at such accident. No such report shall be used as evidence in any trial, civil or criminal, arising out of an accident, except that the police department shall furnish upon demand of any person who has or claims to have made such a report, or upon demand of any court, a certificate showing that a specified accident report has or has not been made to the department. 
(Code 1996, § 8-1-10) 
Sec. 8-1-11. - Reserved. 
Sec. 8-1-12. - Reckless operation of bicycles. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to operate any bicycle in the town in a reckless or dangerous manner. 
(Code 1996, § 8-1-12) 
CHAPTER 2. - TRAFFIC REGULATIONS 

Sec. 8-2-1. - Obedience to official traffic-control devices. 
(a)  The driver of any vehicle shall obey the instructions of any official traffic-control device applicable thereto placed in accordance with the traffic ordinances of the town, unless otherwise directed by a police officer, subject to the exceptions granted to the driver of an authorized emergency vehicle in this chapter. 
(b)  No provision of this chapter for which signs are required shall be enforced against an alleged violator if, at the time and place of the alleged violation, an official sign is not in proper position and sufficiently legible to be seen by an ordinarily observant person. 
(Code 1996, § 8-2-1) 
Sec. 8-2-2. - Display of unauthorized signs, signals or markers. 
(a)  No person shall place, maintain or display upon or in view of any street any unauthorized sign, signal, marking or device which purports to be, or is an imitation of, or resembles an official traffic-control device or railroad sign or signal, or which attempts to direct the movement of traffic, or which hides from view or interferes with the effectiveness of any official traffic-control device, sign or signal. 
(b)  No person shall place or maintain, nor shall any public authority permit, any commercial advertising on any traffic sign or signal. 
(c)  Every such prohibited sign, signal or marking is hereby declared to be a public nuisance, and the authority having jurisdiction over the street is hereby empowered to remove the same or cause it to be removed without notice. 
(Code 1996, § 8-2-2) 
Sec. 8-2-3. - Interference with traffic-control devices, signs, etc. 
    No person shall, without lawful authority, attempt to alter, deface, injure, knock down or remove any official traffic-control device or any railroad sign or signal. 
(Code 1996, § 8-2-3) 
Sec. 8-2-4. - Zones of quiet. 
    Whenever authorized signs are erected indicating a zone of quiet, no person operating a motor vehicle within any such zone shall sound the horn or other warning device of such vehicle, except in an emergency. 
(Code 1996, § 8-2-4) 
Sec. 8-2-5. - Driving through private driveways, filling stations, etc. 
(a)  No vehicle shall be driven through or across any private driveway or filling station premises for the purpose of avoiding any traffic-control device. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person driving a vehicle to make any U-turn or other turn prohibited at any point where such turn is prohibited, and it shall be unlawful to accomplish a U-turn by deviously going into or through private property adjoining the street where such turn is prohibited. 
(Code 1996, § 8-2-5) 
Sec. 8-2-6. - Stop when traffic obstructed. 
    No driver shall enter an intersection or a marked crosswalk unless there is sufficient space on the other side of the intersection or crosswalk to accommodate the vehicle he is operating without obstructing the passage of other vehicles or pedestrians, notwithstanding any traffic-control signal indication to proceed. 
(Code 1996, § 8-2-6) 
Sec. 8-2-7. - Funeral processions. 
(a)  A funeral procession of vehicles shall be identified by the display of lights on each vehicle and as may be further designated by the traffic division of the police department. 
(b)  Each driver in a funeral procession shall drive as near to the right-hand edge of the roadway as practical and follow the vehicle ahead as close as is practical and safe. 
(Code 1996, § 8-2-7) 
Sec. 8-2-8. - Driving through funeral processions. 
    No driver of a vehicle shall drive between the vehicles comprising a funeral or other authorized procession while they are in motion and when such vehicles are conspicuously designated as required in section 8-2-7. This provision shall not apply at intersections where traffic is controlled by traffic-control signals or police officers. 
(Code 1996, § 8-2-8) 
Sec. 8-2-9. - Duties regarding pedestrians. 
    Every driver of a vehicle shall exercise due care to avoid colliding with any pedestrian upon any roadway, and shall give warning by sounding the horn when necessary, and shall exercise proper precaution upon observing any child or any confused or incapacitated person upon a roadway. 
(Code 1996, § 8-2-9) 
CHAPTER 3. - STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING 

Sec. 8-3-1. - Compliance with signs. 
    Where signs prohibiting or restricting parking are erected on any street, no person shall park a vehicle in violation thereof. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-1) 
Sec. 8-3-2. - Parking prohibited in certain places. 
(a)  No person shall stop, stand or park any vehicle upon a street, other than an alley, in such a manner or under such conditions as to leave available less than ten feet of the width of the roadway for free movement of vehicle traffic, except that a driver may stop temporarily during the actual loading or unloading of passengers or when necessary in obedience to traffic regulations or traffic signs or signals of a police officer. 
(b)  No person shall park a vehicle within an alley in such a manner or under such conditions as to leave available less than ten feet of the width of the roadway for the free movement of vehicular traffic. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-2) 
Sec. 8-3-3. - Standing or parking close to curb. 
(a)  No person shall stand or park a vehicle in a roadway other than parallel with the right edge of the roadway, headed in the direction of traffic, and with the curb-side wheels of the vehicle within 12 inches of the edge of the roadway, except that upon those streets which have been marked or signed for angle parking, vehicles shall be parked at the angle to the curb indicated by such mark or signs. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person or group of persons to congregate upon the streets or sidewalks of the town in such a manner as to impede the free flow of traffic. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-3) 
Sec. 8-3-4. - Parking for display, repairs, etc. 
    No person shall stand or park a vehicle upon any roadway for the principal purpose of: 
(1)  Displaying it for sale; or 
(2)  Washing, greasing or repairing such vehicle, except repairs necessitated by an emergency. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-4) 
Sec. 8-3-5. - Loading and unloading at rear or side of business. 
    All persons loading or unloading goods at any business or any establishment in a business district shall use back or side entrances where they are accessible, and where there exists an accessible back or side entrance, it shall be unlawful to load or unload goods across any sidewalk of the principal business streets of the town. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-5) 
Sec. 8-3-6. - Owner responsible for illegal parking. 
    No person shall allow or permit any vehicle registered in his name to stand or park in any street in the town in violation of any of the ordinances of the town regulating the standing or parking of vehicles. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-6) 
Sec. 8-3-7. - Time parking. 
    When signs are erected giving notice thereof, no person shall park a vehicle for longer than stated time between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m. of any day, except Sundays and public holidays. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-7) 
Sec. 8-3-8. - Double parking. 
    It shall be unlawful for any operator of any of the above means of conveyance to double park within the town limits. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-8) 
Sec. 8-3-9. - Trailers. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to park any trailer coach of any kind overnight on any street, alley, highway or other public place. 
(b)  No trailer coach shall be parked or located and used or occupied on any tract of land other than within an authorized trailer coach park, except: 
(1)  Trailer coaches which were located on their present sites prior to January 1, 1993; 
(2)  Trailer coaches used as offices, on a temporary basis, by contractors making application for a temporary parking permit to the town clerk-treasurer for a period not to exceed three months, renewable upon approval by town council; 
(3)  Trailers used as temporary (maximum of six months) office space pending completion of a permanent office space. No such temporary permit will be issued unless there is positive evidence that a permanent office is to be constructed; and 
(4)  Camper trailers, campers mountable on other vehicles and mobile camper units so long as they shall remain unoccupied. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-9) 
Sec. 8-3-10. - Marking of curbs or streets; parking within lines required. 
    Lines or markings shall be painted or placed upon the curb or upon the street for the purpose of designating the confines of the parking space, and each vehicle parking in any such parking space shall park within the lines or markings as established. It shall be unlawful to park any vehicle across any such line or marking or in such position that the same shall not be entirely within the area so designated by such lines or markings. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-10) 
Sec. 8-3-11. - Handicapped parking. 
(a)  The town council shall designate the number and location of handicapped parking zones within the town and the time limit for parking in such zones and shall provide for appropriate signs and markings indicating same. 
(b)  Those persons who have obtained a placard or license plate from the state department of highways and public transportation pursuant to S.C. Code 1976, § 56-3-1960, shall be entitled to park their vehicles in spaces designated for handicapped parking, and when so parked, shall not be subject to the fines and penalties imposed by this chapter. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-11) 
State Law reference- Handicapped parking, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-3-1950 et seq. 
Sec. 8-3-12. - Violations. 
    Whenever any motor vehicle is found to be in violation of any of the provisions of this chapter, the officer finding it shall take its registration number, license number, and parking meter number, if any, and affix to such vehicle or issue to the driver thereof, if he is present, a notice in writing, on a form to be provided by the town, for the driver to post a specified bond or to answer the charge against him during the hours and at the time and place specified in the notice. The schedule of bonds and fines shall be as fixed from time to time by the town council. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-12) 
Sec. 8-3-13. - Removal of abandoned, wrecked or illegally parked vehicles. 
(a)  Removal of vehicle conditions. Whenever a police officer finds a vehicle that has been abandoned or wrecked upon the public streets or ways of the town, or that has been parked in violation of a town ordinance or state law, or the vehicle has been or is being used in commission of a crime, such officer may, with the approval of the chief of police, have such vehicle removed by a wrecker to the storage lot or garage operated by such owner. Vehicles removed under the above conditions shall be held until claimed by the legal owner or otherwise disposed of as provided by law. 
(b)  Wrecker and towing services generally . Wreckers are to go to an accident only when properly called. It shall be unlawful for the owner or agent of any wrecker or towing service to go to any place within the town where an accident has occurred unless called by the owner of the vehicle involved, or his authorized representative, or an authorized representative of the town. 
(c)  Solicitation of wrecker or towing service . It shall be unlawful for the owner or agent of any wrecker or towing service to drive along or park on any streets, bridges, or highways within the town for the sole purpose of soliciting wrecker or towing service. 
(d)  Solicitation of business by town employees prohibited . It shall be unlawful for any town employee to solicit business for any wrecker or towing service. 
(e)  Rules and regulations . In order to be eligible to be placed on the towing list: 
(1)  All wrecker or towing services must have a wrecker available at all times (24 hours a day, seven days a week). 
(2)  The wrecker or towing service must have been in business for 12 calendar months before being placed on the list. 
(3)  Said business must also be in the corporate limits of the town or have a valid town business license. 
(4)  Unless specified by the owner of the vehicle at the time it is being towed, all vehicles towed must be stored within the town limits of the town. 
(5)  Said service must comply with all sections of this chapter, all rules listed and any other additional rules the police department deems necessary to safeguard vehicles in their custody. 
(6)  Towing agreement with each wrecker or towing services will be operated on a rotating basis. 
(7)  The wrecker or towing service will be responsible for all damage or loss on all vehicles, unless such loss or damage is noted by police officer before the vehicle is removed from the scene. The wrecker or towing service towing for the town will be responsible for pointing out damage to the vehicle before leaving the scene. 
(8)  All wrecker and towing services must conform to and comply with all town building codes and business license ordinances pertaining to such services. 
(9)  The town shall have the authority to adopt from time to time reasonable rules and regulations, including establishing zones or contracts for the operation of wreckers for town towing. 
(f)  Penalty . Any person, firm or corporation or agent who shall violate a provision of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and, upon conviction, such persons shall be punished by a fine of not more than $500.00 and imprisoned for not more than 30 days for each offense. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-13) 
State Law reference- Removal of abandoned vehicles from highways, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-5610 et seq.; authority of police to remove illegally parked vehicles, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-2520. 
Sec. 8-3-14. - Storage and wrecker charges. 
    Storage and wrecker charges shall be imposed on vehicles seized pursuant to section 8-3-13, in accordance with the rotation of the wrecker. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-14) 
Sec. 8-3-15. - Release of vehicle to owner. 
    No impounded vehicle shall be released until all towing, storage and other charges have been paid, proper evidence of ownership has been exhibited and the police issue discharge papers. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-15) 
Sec. 8-3-16. - Fire lane parking. 
(a)  There will be no parking in an area marked as a fire lane, except for emergency vehicles. Anyone who violates this section will be subject to a fine of not less than $10.00 or more than $100.00. 
(b)  A fire lane must be properly marked with signs and a painted area no less than 18 feet from a building. When on private property, this property must be properly posted as to state and local ordinances. 
(Code 1996, § 8-3-16) 
State Law reference- Parking lots in police jurisdiction, S.C. Code 1976, § 23-1-15; powers of local authorities, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-710 
CHAPTER 4. - JUNK AND WRECKED MOTOR VEHICLES 

Sec. 8-4-1. - Prohibition of junk vehicles. 
    The relevant provisions of the International Property Maintenance Code, adopted by reference, apply to the prohibition of junk vehicles. 
(Ord. of 12-13-2010(04)) 
Sec. 8-4-2. - Defined. 
    For the purpose of this chapter, a vehicle shall be determined to have been abandoned under one or more of the following circumstances: 
(1)  Left upon a street or highway in violation of a law or ordinance controlling traffic or prohibiting parking; 
(2)  Failing to display a current license plate; 
(3)  Partially dismantled or damaged and left out of doors, in an uncovered, unscreened or unenclosed state; 
(4)  Incapable of self propulsion or being moved in the manner for which it was originally intended and left out of doors, in an uncovered, unscreened or unenclosed state; 
(5)  Left on property owned or operated by the town without its consent, other than a street or right-of-way, for a period in excess of 24 hours; 
(6)  Left on private property without the consent of the owner, occupant or lessee thereof for a period in excess of 24 hours; or 
(7)  Left on any public street or right-of-way of the town for a period in excess of seven days. 
(Code 1996, § 8-4-2) 
Sec. 8-4-3. - Removal. 
    The person responsible, or the registered owner of any vehicle if it can be determined after a reasonable search, or the owner of the premises on which the vehicle is located, or all, shall be given notice as prescribed in this chapter to remove and dispose of an abandoned vehicle at his own expense, or he shall be in violation of this chapter. 
(1)  If the person or owner cannot be determined or has not complied within the time prescribed by the notice, the vehicle, if located on public property, at the discretion of the town, may be removed to a storage area for safekeeping at the direction of the town. Written notice of the removal shall be promptly given to the registered owner of the vehicle and to any holders of any lien on record in the office of the state department of motor vehicles, if it can be determined after a reasonable search. The town may remove the vehicles without prior notice when the vehicles constitute a safety hazard or other public nuisance. 
(2)  If located on private property, no vehicle shall be so removed from the premises by the town without the written authorization of the owner of the vehicle, if known, or the owner, lessee or occupant of the premises, unless the vehicle has been declared to be a safety hazard or other public nuisance. 
(Code 1996, § 8-4-3) 
Sec. 8-4-4. - Disposition of vehicles. 
(a)  The owner of any removed vehicle, before obtaining possession thereof, shall pay to the town all reasonable costs incidental to its removal, storage or the locating of the owner. 
(b)  Should the owner fail or refuse to pay the costs within 20 days after receipt of the notice, or should his identity or whereabouts be unknown and unascertainable after a reasonable search and after notice as prescribed herein, the stored vehicle may be sold after 20 days' notice has been given to the department of motor vehicles before the date of the sale and after the vehicle has been held for not less than 30 days; provided, further, that section 8-4-5 shall govern the disposition of any junk motor vehicles. 
(c)  The vehicle may be sold by public sale, after one public notice, but no vehicle may be sold or disposed of until its value has been determined in writing by at least two disinterested dealers or garagemen. 
(d)  A vehicle of an appraised value of less than $50.00 may be disposed of by any means in the discretion of the storing agent of the town. 
(e)  The proceeds of any sale shall be forwarded to the clerk-treasurer, who shall pay from the proceeds, the costs of removal, storage, investigation as to ownership and sale and other liens, in that order. If after the sale the ownership at the time of removal is established satisfactorily to the clerk-treasurer, the owner shall be paid so much of the proceeds as remains after payment of the foregoing costs and liens; otherwise, any remaining proceeds shall be deposited after 90 days in the general fund of the town. 
(Code 1996, § 8-4-4) 
Sec. 8-4-5. - Junk motor vehicles. 
(a)  Any motor vehicle which does not have lawfully affixed thereto both unexpired license plates and a current motor vehicle safety inspection certificate, and the condition of which is wrecked, dismantled, partially dismantled, inoperative or discarded, and being more than eight years old, shall be deemed a junk motor vehicle. 
(b)  The person responsible, or the owner of the premises on which the vehicle is located, or the registered owner of the vehicle if it can be determined after reasonable search, or all, shall be given notice as prescribed in this chapter to remove and dispose of the vehicle at his own expense, or he shall be in violation of this chapter. If the person or owner cannot be determined or has not complied within the time prescribed by the notice, any vehicle at the discretion of the town may be removed from public property to a storage area for safekeeping at the direction of the town. No vehicle shall be so removed from privately owned premises without the written authorization of the registered owner of the vehicle, if known, or the owner, lessee or occupant of the premises, unless the vehicle has been declared to be a safety hazard or other public nuisance. The costs of its removal and disposal may be assessed against the person responsible for the nuisance, and the costs may be placed as a lien against his property. 
(c)  A junk motor vehicle may be posted in place, and its owner may reclaim it by exhibiting reasonable proof of ownership and paying all reasonable costs incident to its removal, storage and administrative expenses. An unclaimed junk motor vehicle may be destroyed or otherwise disposed of in summary manner after 15 days following possession of the vehicle under the provisions of this chapter. Notice shall be promptly given after final disposition to the state department of motor vehicles on the forms as it provides, that it was deemed a junk motor vehicle and disposed as a junk motor vehicle. This notice shall fully and accurately describe the vehicle. Any proceeds derived from the disposition of junk motor vehicles shall be deposited in the general fund of the town. 
(Code 1996, § 8-4-5) 
Sec. 8-4-6. - Disposition with owner's consent. 
    With a vehicle owner's written consent, the town, at its own discretion, may remove and immediately dispose of any vehicle as a junk motor vehicle regardless of value or condition of the vehicle and without waiting the aforesaid periods. Costs may be assessed to the vehicle owner. 
(Code 1996, § 8-4-6) 
Title 9 - OFFENSES 
CHAPTER 1. - GENERAL PROVISIONS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Fortune-telling to promote business, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-17-690; coin-operated devices, S.C. Code 1976, § 12-21-2710 et seq.; unlawful games and betting, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-19-40; removal of doors from abandoned airtight containers, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-3-1010; open and unprotected abandoned wells, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-3-1020. 

Sec. 9-1-1. - Aiding or abetting. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to counsel, advise, incite, abet, procure or aid any other person in the violation of any of the ordinances of the town. 
(Code 1996, § 9-1-1) 
Sec. 9-1-2. - Establishment of cemetery. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to establish or use, within the town, any place for the burial of the dead without permission of the town council. This prohibition shall not extend to burial grounds established in the town as of the effective date of this Code, within the boundaries established for that purpose. 
(Code 1996, § 9-1-2) 
Secs. 9-1-3-9-1-6. - Reserved. 
Sec. 9-1-7. - Public nuisances. 
(a)  The keeping, maintaining, operation, or control of any building, premises, or condition in a manner that is detrimental to the peace, good order, happiness, safety, or good morals of people living nearby, or of the public generally, constitutes a public nuisance and is hereby forbidden. Each day the conditions continue constitutes a separate offense. 
(b)  In addition, any nuisance may be abated by the town court pursuant to a resolution adopted after a hearing of which all interested parties shall have five days' written notice. 
(Code 1996, § 9-1-7) 
Sec. 9-1-8. - Peddling on public property. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or otherwise carry on a business in the town from the public streets or sidewalks or other public property; provided that this section shall not in any way infringe upon the rights of individuals to have free movement within said town while engaged in any legal business activity or for any other reason. This section shall not in any way prohibit a merchant with a place of business abutting any sidewalk from exhibiting merchandise on the sidewalk immediately in front of such business establishment, provided that such merchant shall not inhibit, prevent or substantially interfere with the free flow of pedestrian traffic on said sidewalk. 
(Code 1996, § 9-1-8) 
Sec. 9-1-9. - Reserved. 
Sec. 9-1-10. - Prohibited obstruction in public places. 
(a)  No person shall loiter or sleep in or upon any street, park or public place or in any public building, or obstruct the access to any public building or any part thereof, or obstruct passage through or upon any public street, park or public place or private property that has been properly posted to show property under the jurisdiction of the town police department. 
(b)  For the purposes of this section, the term "loiter" shall encompass, but not necessarily be limited to, one or more of the following acts: 
(1)  Obstruction of the free unhampered passage of pedestrians or vehicles. 
(2)  Obstructing, molesting or interfering with any person lawfully upon any street, park or other public place. 
(3)  Refusing to move on when so requested by a peace officer, provided that the peace officer has exercised his discretion reasonably under the circumstances in order to preserve or promote public peace and order. 
(c)  For the purpose of this section, the term "other public place" shall be deemed to include the quasi-public area in front or adjacent to any store, shop, restaurant, luncheonette or other place of business and shall include also any parking lots or other vacant private property not owned or under the dominion of the person charged with a violation of this section. 
(Code 1996, § 9-1-10) 
Sec. 9-1-11. - Reserved. 
Sec. 9-1-12. - Placing, extending signs, banners across public way or place. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to extend any banner or canvas sign across any public street, park or other public way or place without first having obtained a permit from the state highway department. 
(Code 1996, § 9-1-12) 
Sec. 9-1-13. - Posting on public property. 
    It shall be unlawful to place any advertisement, business, political or otherwise, or any notice or sign of any nature on public property within the town, by the use of a placard, picture, paper, circular, printing, or by any means or device whatsoever. 
(Code 1996, § 9-1-13) 
Sec. 9-1-14. - Posting property in which town has interest or regulatory power. 
    It shall be unlawful to place any advertisement, notice or sign of any nature or property in which the town has an interest or the right to regulate, such as telephone poles, telegraph poles, electric poles or towers, and the like thereof. 
(Code 1996, § 9-1-14) 
Sec. 9-1-15. - Posting on private property. 
    It shall be unlawful to place any advertisement, notice or sign of any nature on private property, without written consent of the owner or lessee of the property. 
(Code 1996, § 9-1-15) 
Sec. 9-1-16. - Placing handbills in or upon automobiles. 
    No person shall place or cause any commercial handbill to be placed within or upon, or under the windshield wiper of any private automobile parked upon any of the public streets or in any public parking area. This shall not preclude the delivery of any handbill to an owner, occupant or person present and in charge of a vehicle willing to accept and receive the handbill. 
(Code 1996, § 9-1-16) 
Sec. 9-1-17. - Using vehicle for primary purpose of advertising prohibited. 
    No person shall operate or park on any street any vehicle for the primary purpose of advertising. 
(Code 1996, § 9-1-17) 
CHAPTER 2. - OFFENSES AGAINST THE PUBLIC PEACE[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Pointing firearms, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-23-410; concealed weapons, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-23-460; unlawful carrying of pistol, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-23-20; wearing masks, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-7-110; burning crosses, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-7-120; engaging in riot, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-5-120; disturbance of religious worship, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-17-520; disorderly conduct, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-17-530. 

Sec. 9-2-1. - Assault and battery. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to commit an assault or assault and battery upon any other person in the town. 
(Code 1996, § 9-2-1) 
Sec. 9-2-2. - Weapons. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to: 
(1)  Negligently or carelessly fire or discharge any firearm, including, but not limited to, any air rifle, pellet gun, pistol, or other device which may be potentially be harmful to any person or property; 
(2)  Draw a knife, gun, pistol or any dangerous or deadly weapon in any fight or disturbance; 
(3)  Publicly brandish a firearm; 
(4)  Carry about the person in the town, whether concealed or not, any dirk, slingshot, metal knuckles, razor or other weapon usually used for the infliction of personal injury; 
(5)  Carry about the person any gun, pistol, or other type firearm whether concealed or not; 
(6)  To shoot or discharge any firearm within the town or have in their possession a firearm not in compliance with state regulations of firearms as to size and weight existing at the time in question. 
(b)  Any person carrying a concealed weapon in violation of subsections (a)(5) or (6) of this section shall forfeit the weapon to the town pursuant to S.C. Code 1976, § 16-23-460 and such weapon may subsequently be sold or otherwise disposed of as provided in S.C. Code 1976, § 16-23-500. 
(c)  This section shall not apply to police or other law enforcement officers while in the exercise and discharge of their duties or to any theatrical or like performance; nor shall it be construed to abridge or abrogate the right of defense of person or property. 
(d)  This section shall not apply to any person who possesses a permit to carry a firearm pursuant to S.C. Code 1976, § 16-23-20(12). Nor shall this section apply to any person who is a licensed hunter or fisherman while engaged in hunting or fishing and going to and from their places of hunting or fishing. 
(Code 1996, § 9-2-2) 
Sec. 9-2-3. - Disruption of court or council. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to interrupt the proceedings of the municipal court or town council, or be guilty of disorderly conduct therein, or to commit any contempt of either. 
(Code 1996, § 9-2-3) 
Sec. 9-2-4. - Fireworks. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person or persons to light, fire, ignite or discharge fireworks within the corporate limits of the Town, except as provided in subsection (b) of this section. For the purposes of this section and the remaining sections of this section, "fireworks" means fireworks as defined by State statutory law including S.C. Code Section 23-35-175 and ICC Class C Common Fireworks as described therein. 
(b)  Exceptions: 
(1)  All town sponsored events are exempt from the provisions of subsection (a) including pyrotechnic companies hired by the town for enjoyment purposes. All pyrotechnic companies shall comply with any and all federal, state and municipal regulations as far as licensing, insurance and pennits. 
(2)  The discharging or shooting of fireworks on the 4th of July between the hours of 10:00 a.m. and 10:00 p.m., unless drought conditions exist and a red flag warning has been issued for the town. 
(3)  The discharging or shooting of fireworks between the hours of 10:00 a.m. on December 31 and 1:00 a.m. on January 1. 
(4)  The discharging or shooting of fireworks in conjunction with a special event to the extent allowed under the terms of the permit issued by town hall, with approval given by the town manager and police chief. 
(5)  The provisions of this section shall not include nor prevent the possession or use of toy cap pistols and toy pistol paper caps which contain no more than twenty hundredths (0.20) of a grain of explosive mixture and fireworks known as sparklers. The use and possession of such toy cap pistols, toy pistol caps and sparklers shall be permitted at all times. 
(c)  Nothing contained in subsection (a) shall be construed as prohibiting the use of signals necessary for the safe operation of buses, trucks, or trains within the town. 
(d)  All fireworks discharged under this provision shall be under the direct supervision of a responsible adult. 
(e)  Enforcement and penalties: 
(1)  A person who uses, fires, shoots, or discharges any fireworks within the corporate limits of the town or fails to comply with the provisions of this section shall be deemed guilty of an infraction for each occurrence of noncompliance. 
(2)  An infraction is punishable by a fine up to the maximum amount allowed by state law. Each occurrence of a violation of this section shall be considered a separate and distinct infraction. A violation of this section is further declared to be a public nuisance. 
(Code 1996, § 9-2-4; Ord. of 2-9-2015) 
State Law reference- Fireworks, S.C. Code 1976, § 23-35-10 et seq. 
Sec. 9-2-5. - Unreasonable noise prohibited. 
    The making or contributing to the creation of any loud or disturbing noise of such character, intensity or duration as to be detrimental to the life, health or discomfort of any ordinary, reasonable person is hereby prohibited. The following acts, among others, are declared to be loud, disturbing noises in violation of this section, but enumeration shall not be deemed to be exclusive. 
(1)  The sounding or blowing of any horn or signal device on any automobile, motorcycle, motor bus or other vehicle, except as a danger signal if another vehicle is approaching apparently out of control, or, if in motion, only as a danger signal; the creation by any signal device of any loud or harsh noise; and the sounding of such device for any unnecessary period of time. 
(2)  The playing of any radio, phonograph, piccolo, television or any musical instrument, including radios, cassette players, and CD players in motor vehicles, in such a manner or with such volume as to disturb any person, or the playing of such instrument in such manner as to annoy or disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of any ordinary, reasonable person in any dwelling, hotel, or other residences. 
(3)  The keeping of any animal or bird which by causing frequency of long continued noise shall disturb comfort or repose of any ordinary, reasonable person in the vicinity. 
(4)  The use of any automobile, motorcycle or vehicle so out of repair, so loaded, or used or repaired in such manner, as to create loud noises, particularly grating, grinding, rattling, riveting or other disturbing noises. 
(5)  The blowing of any steam whistle attached to any stationary boiler, except to give notice to the time to begin or stop work or as a warning of danger. 
(6)  The discharge into the open air of the exhaust from any steam engine, stationary internal combustion engine, motor boat engine or motor vehicle, except through a muffler or other device which will effectively prevent loud or explosive noises therefrom. 
(7)  The use of any mechanical device operated by compressed air, unless the noise created thereby is effectively muffled and reduced. 
(8)  The erection, including excavation, demolition, alteration or repair of any building in a residential or business district other than between the hours of 6:00 a.m. and 10:00 p.m. on weekdays, except in cases of urgent necessity in the interest of public safety. 
(9)  The creation of any excessive noise on any street adjacent to any school, institution of learning, library, or court while the same is in session or adjacent to any church during church services which interferes with the work or worship in any such place or institution, provided that signs must be displayed in such streets indicating that the same is a school, church, library, or court. 
(10)  The creation of loud and excessive noises in connection with loading or unloading any vehicle, or opening and destroying bales, boxes, crates and containers. 
(11)  The sounding of any bell or gong attached to any building or premises, which disturbs the quiet or repose of any ordinary, reasonable person in the vicinity thereof. 
(12)  The shouting, loud talking, crying or soliciting by peddlers, hawkers, solicitors and vendors which disturbs the quiet and peace of the neighborhood. 
(13)  The use of any drum, loudspeaker or other instrument or device for the purpose of attracting attention to any performance or event, show, sale or the display or advertisement of merchandise, by the creation of noise. 
(14)  The use of any mechanical loudspeakers or amplifiers on trucks, airplanes or other vehicles for advertising or other purposes. 
(15)  The operation of any garage, filling station, auto repair business, taxicab business, plant, store, factory or other place of business, between the hours of 9:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m., in such manner as to create loud and disturbing noises, of such frequency or such frequency or such volume as to disturb the quiet and comfort of any ordinary, reasonable citizen. 
(Code 1996, § 9-2-5) 
Sec. 9-2-6. - Disorderly conduct. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in disorderly conduct, which shall consist of any one or more of the following: 
(1)  Acting in a violent or tumultuous manner toward another, whereby any person is placed in danger of his life, limb or health; 
(2)  Acting in a violent or tumultuous manner toward another, whereby the property of any person is placed in danger of being destroyed or damaged; 
(3)  Causing, provoking or engaging in any fight, brawl or riotous conduct so as to endanger the life, limb, health or property of another; 
(4)  Using fighting words directed toward any person who thereby becomes outraged and thus creates a turmoil; 
(5)  Congregating with another or others in or on any public way so as to halt the flow of vehicular or pedestrian traffic, and refuse to clear such public way when ordered by the town public safety officers or other lawful authority; 
(6)  Being drunk or under the influence of alcohol, or any narcotic or hypnotic drug or any stimulant or depressant on any street or public place to such an extent as to jeopardize persons or property or as to menace the public peace and safety. 
(7)  Endangering lawful pursuits of another by acts of violence, angry threats and abusive conduct. 
(8)  Assembling or congregating with another or others for the purpose of causing, provoking or engaging in any fight or brawl. 
(9)  Being found jostling or roughly crowding or pushing in any public place. 
(10)  Collecting in bodies or in crowds for unlawful purposes. 
(11)  Assembling or congregating with another or others, for the purpose of, or with the intent to engage in, gaming. 
(12)  Frequenting any public place with intent to obtain money from another by an illegal and fraudulent scheme, trick, artifice or device. 
(13)  Assembling with another or others for the purpose of engaging in any fraudulent scheme, device or trick to obtain any valuable thing in any place or from any person in the town, or who shall aid or abet therein. 
(14)  Uttering, while in a state of anger, in the presence of another any lewd or obscene words. 
(15)  Frequenting any place where gaming or illegal sale or possession of alcoholic beverages or narcotics or dangerous drug is practiced, allowed or tolerated. 
(16)  Any person who shall act in a dangerous manner toward others. 
(17)  Assembling or congregating with another or other person for the purpose of doing bodily harm to another. 
(18)  Acting in a violent manner that interferes with another's pursuit of a lawful occupation. 
(19)  Being found on any highway or at any public place or public gathering in a grossly intoxicated condition. 
(b)  This section shall not apply to peaceful picketing, public speaking or other lawful expressions of opinion not in contravention of other laws. 
(c)  Any person convicted of violating any provision of this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1996, § 9-2-6) 
Sec. 9-2-7. - Interfering with law enforcement officers. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully fail or refuse to comply with any lawful order or direction of any law enforcement officer, or to otherwise interfere with, impede, hinder or resist any such officer in the discharge of his duties. Speech alone that questions or expresses opposition to action by law enforcement personnel does not constitute a violation of this section. 
(Code 1996, § 9-2-7) 
State Law reference- Hindering officers, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-5-50; resisting arrest, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-9-320. 
Sec. 9-2-8. - Possession of open containers while on public streets and sidewalks. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to have in his possession any opened container containing beer, ale, porter, wine or other similar malt or fermented beverage, or other alcoholic liquor or any mixture thereof by whatever name called or known which contains alcohol and is used as a beverage, while on any public street or sidewalk. 
(Code 1996, § 9-2-8) 
Sec. 9-2-9. - Drunkenness in public place. 
    No person shall be drunk or intoxicated in any street, public house, place of amusement or worship, or any public place in the town. 
(Code 1996, § 9-2-9) 
Sec. 9-2-10. - Drug paraphernalia. 
(a)  Definitions . The following sections of this chapter will coincide with existing federal, state and city laws. The term "drug paraphernalia" means all equipment, products and material of any kind which are used, intended for use or designed for use in planting, propagating, cultivating, growing, harvesting, manufacturing, compounding, converting, producing, processing, preparing, testing, analyzing, packaging, repackaging, storing, containing, concealing, injecting, ingesting, inhaling, or otherwise introducing into the human body a controlled substance in violation of this Act (meaning the Controlled Substances Act of the state). It includes, but is not limited to: 
(1)  Kits used, intended for use, or designed for use, in planting, propagating, cultivating, growing or harvesting of any species of plant which is a controlled substance or from which a controlled substance can be derived; 
(2)  Kits used, intended for use or designed for use, in manufacturing, compounding, converting, producing, processing, or preparing controlled substances; 
(3)  Isomerizating devices used, intended for use or designed for use, in increasing the potency of any species of plant which is a controlled substance; 
(4)  Testing equipment used, intended for use or designed for use, in identifying or in analyzing the strength, effectiveness of purity of controlled substances; 
(5)  Scales and balances used, intended for use or designed for use, in weighing or measuring controlled substances; 
(6)  Diluents and adulterants, such as quinine hydrochloride, mannitol, mannite, dextrose and lactose, used, intended for use or designed for use, in cutting controlled substances; 
(7)  Separating gins and sifters used, intended for use or designed for use, in removing twigs and seeds from, or in otherwise cleaning or refining marijuana; 
(8)  Blenders, bowls, containers, spoons and mixing devices used, intended for use or designed for use, in compounding controlled substances; 
(9)  Capsules, balloons, envelopes and other containers used, intended for use or designed for use, in packaging small quantities of controlled substances; 
(10)  Containers and other objects used, intended for use, or designed for use in storing or concealing controlled substances; 
(11)  Hypodermic syringes, needles and other objects used, intended for use or designed for use, in parenterally injected controlled substances into the human body; 
(12)  Objects used, intended for use or designed for use, in ingesting, inhaling, or otherwise introducing marijuana, cocaine, hashish, or hashish oil into the human body, such as: 
a.  Metal, wooden, acrylic, glass, stone, plastic, or ceramic pipes with or without screens, hashish heads, or punctured metal bowls; 
b.  Water pipes; 
c.  Carburetion tubes and devices; 
d.  Smoking and carburetion masks; 
e.  Roach clips, meaning objects used to hold burning material, such as a marihuana cigarette, that has become too small or too short to be held in the hand; 
f.  Miniature cocaine spoons and cocaine vials; 
g.  Chamber pipes; 
h.  Carburetor pipes; 
i.  Electric pipes; 
j.  Air-driven pipes; 
k.  Chillums; 
l.  Bongs; 
m.  Ice pipes or chillers. 
(b)  Determination of object as drug paraphernalia. In determining whether an object is drug paraphernalia, a court or other authority should consider, in addition to all other logically relevant factors, the following: 
(1)  Statements by an owner or by anyone in control of the object concerning its use; 
(2)  Prior convictions, if any, of an owner, or of anyone in control of the object, under any state or federal law relating to any controlled substance; 
(3)  The proximity of the object, in time and space, to a direct violation of this section; 
(4)  The proximity of the object to controlled substances; 
(5)  The existence of any residue of controlled substances on the object. 
(6)  Direct or circumstantial evidence of the intent of an owner, or of anyone in control of the object, to deliver it to persons whom he knows, or should reasonable know, intend to use the object to facilitate a violation of this section; the innocence of an owner, or of anyone in control of the object, as to a direct violation of this section should not prevent a finding that the object is intended for use, or designed for use, as drug paraphernalia; 
(7)  Instructions, oral or written, provided with the object concerning its use; 
(8)  Descriptive materials accompanying the object which explain or depict its use; 
(9)  National and local advertising concerning its use; 
(10)  The manner in which the object is displayed for sale; 
(11)  Whether the owner or anyone in control of the object is a legitimate supplier of like or related items to the community such as a licensed distributor or dealer of tobacco products; 
(12)  Direct or circumstantial evidence of the ratio of sales of the object to the total sales of the business enterprise; 
(13)  The existence and scope of legitimate uses for the object in the community; 
(14)  Expert testimony concerning its use. 
(c)  Offenses and penalties . 
(1)  Possession of drug paraphernalia . It is unlawful for any person to use, or to possess with intent to use, drug paraphernalia to plant, propagate, cultivate, grow, harvest, manufacture, compound, convert, produce, process, prepare, test, analyze, pack, repack, store, contain, conceal, inject, ingest, inhale, or otherwise introduce into the human body a controlled substance in violation of this section. Any person who violates this section is guilty of a crime and, upon conviction, may be imprisoned for not more than 30 days, fined not more than $500.00, or both. 
(2)  Manufacture or delivery of drug paraphernalia . It is unlawful for any person to deliver, possess with intent to deliver, or manufacture with intent to deliver, drug paraphernalia, knowing, or under circumstances where one reasonably should know, that it will be used to plant, propagate, cultivate, grow, harvest, manufacture, compound, convert, produce, process, prepare, test, analyze, pack, repack, store, contain, conceal, inject, inhale or otherwise introduce into the human body a controlled substance in violation of this Act. Any person who violates this section is guilty of a crime and upon conviction may be imprisoned for not more than 30 days, fined not more than $500.00, or both. 
(3)  Delivery of drug paraphernalia . Any person 18 years of age or over who violates the above section by delivering drug paraphernalia to a person under 18 years of age who is at least three years his junior is guilty of a special offense and upon conviction may be imprisoned for not more than 30 days, fined not more than $500.00, or both. 
(4)  Advertisement of drug paraphernalia . It is unlawful for any person to place in any newspaper, magazine, handbill, or other publication any advertisement, knowing, or under circumstances where one reasonably should know, that the purpose of the advertisement, in whole or in part, is to promote the sale of objects designed or intended for use as drug paraphernalia. Any person who violates this section is guilty of a crime and, upon conviction, may be imprisoned for not more than 30 days, fined not more than $500.00, or both. 
(d)  Civil forfeiture . All drug paraphernalia, as defined by subsection (a) of this section, are subject to forfeiture. 
(e)  Severability . If any provision of this section or the application thereof to any person or circumstance is held invalid, the invalidity does not affect other provisions or applications of the section which can be given effect without the invalid provision or application and to this end the provisions of this section are severable. 
(Code 1996, § 9-2-10) 
CHAPTER 3. - OFFENSES AGAINST PROPERTY[3]

Sec. 9-3-1. - Property; injuring damaging, destroying, etc. 
(a)  Generally. It shall be unlawful for any person to destroy, damage, mutilate or remove the property of another. The following acts, among others, are declared to be in violation of this section, but this enumeration shall not be deemed to be exclusive. 
(1)  Personal property . No person within the town shall willfully, unlawfully and maliciously cut, shoot, maim, wound or otherwise injure any personal property of another person. 
(2)  Fixtures and real property . No person within the town shall willfully, unlawfully or maliciously cut, mutilate, deface or otherwise injure any tree, house, outside fence or fixture of another, or commit any other trespass upon real property in the possession of another. 
(3)  Municipal property . No person within the town, unless authorized by town officials, shall remove, interfere with or destroy any town property. 
(4)  Grassplots, flowers, etc . No person shall drive any animal or vehicle along, on or across any grass plot in any street, public place or sidewalk, or to trample, pluck, mutilate or injure the grass, shrubs or flowers planted or growing in such place. 
(5)  Trees and shrubs . No person shall cut, scar, mutilate, dig up or otherwise injure or destroy any trees or shrubs on the public streets or in the parks of the town. 
(b)  Violations. Any person violating the terms of this section shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1996, § 9-3-1) 
Sec. 9-3-2. - Reserved. 
Sec. 9-3-3. - Trespassing upon private property. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to go upon the property of another without the invitation or permission of the owner. Any person found upon the property of another without the owner's consent or permission, shall be guilty of trespassing and subject to a fine not exceeding $500.00 or imprisonment of not more than 30 days, or both. 
(Code 1996, § 9-3-3) 
Sec. 9-3-4. - Throwing trash upon private property. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to throw trash, litter or waste of any kind upon the private property of another without the permission of the owner, lessee or occupant of the said property. 
(Code 1996, § 9-3-4) 
CHAPTER 4. - OFFENSES AGAINST MORALITY[4]

Sec. 9-4-1. - Solicitation for illegal purposes. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to invite or entice any person upon any street, public square or enclosure in the town to accompany, go with or follow such person to any place for illegal purposes, or to invite, entice or address any person from any door, window, porch or portico of any house or building, or to enter any house, or go with or accompany such person to any place for illegal purposes. 
(Code 1996, § 9-4-1) 
Title 10 - OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES 
CHAPTER 1. - PROCUREMENT PROCEDURES 

Sec. 10-1-1. - Procurement code adopted. 
    Procurement procedures in this chapter and regulations hereby authorized are adopted pursuant to S.C. Code 1976, § 11-35-50, and may be cited as "The Town Procurement Code." Terms used in this procurement code shall be defined in accordance with S.C. Code 1976, § 11-35-310. 
(Code 1996, § 10-1-1) 
Sec. 10-1-2. - Purchasing agent. 
    The town manager shall appoint a purchasing agent, who shall serve at his pleasure and be subject to the finance director. The purchasing agent of a designated department head shall be responsible for procurement under the regulations promulgated by the town manager. 
(Code 1996, § 10-1-2) 
Sec. 10-1-3. - Public access to procurement information. 
    Procurement information shall be a public record to the extent required by chapter 3 of title 30 (The Freedom of Information Act), Code of Laws of South Carolina, 1976, as amended, with the exception that commercial or financial information obtained in response to a request for proposals which is privileged and confidential need not be disclosed. 
(Code 1996, § 10-1-3) 
Sec. 10-1-4. - Compliance with federal requirements. 
    Where a procurement involves the expenditure of federal assistance or contract funds, the town shall also comply with such federal law and authorized regulations as are mandatorily applicable. Notwithstanding, where federal assistance or contract funds are used in a procurement, requirements of this Code and town regulations that are more restrictive than federal requirements shall be followed. 
(Code 1996, § 10-1-4) 
Sec. 10-1-5. - Methods of source selection. 
    All town contracts shall be awarded by competitive sealed bidding, except the following as determined pursuant to definitions and standards set by regulations: 
(1)  Professional services where the person employed is customarily employed on a fee basis rather than by competitive bidding (example: appraiser, architect-engineer, auditor, legal service, physician); 
(2)  Competitive sealed proposals; 
(3)  Negotiations after unsuccessful competitive sealed bidding; 
(4)  Small purchases; 
(5)  Sole source procurements; 
(6)  Emergency procurements; 
(7)  Procurement of information technology; 
(8)  Leasing of real property for governmental use; 
(9)  When purchasing through state contracts. 
(Code 1996, § 10-1-5) 
Sec. 10-1-6. - Bidding procedures. 
    Regulations promulgated by the town manager shall provide for fair and equitable procurement system for the town through one or more of the following methods: 
(1)  Competitive sealed bidding; 
(2)  Competitive sealed proposals; 
(3)  Negotiations after unsuccessful competitive sealed bidding; 
(4)  Small purchases; 
(5)  Sole source procurement; 
(6)  Emergency procurements; 
(7)  Negotiations for contracts exempted from competitive procurement. 
(Code 1996, § 10-1-6) 
Sec. 10-1-7. - Correction or withdrawal of bids. 
(a)  Cancellation of awards . Correction or withdrawal of inadvertently erroneous bids before bid opening, withdrawal of inadvertently erroneous bids after award, or cancellation of awards of contracts based on such bid mistakes, may be permitted in accordance with regulations promulgated by the town manager. After bid opening, no change in bid prices or other provisions of bids prejudicial to the interest of the town or fair competition shall be permitted. All decisions to permit the correction or withdrawal of bids or to cancel awards or contracts based on bid mistakes, shall be supported by a written determination of appropriateness and shall be subject to approval by the town council when the amount involved exceeds $5,000.00. 
(b)  Tie bids . In the event two or more bidders are tied in price while otherwise meeting all of the required conditions, awards are determined as follows: 
(1)  Should there be a town firm tied with an out-of-town firm, the award shall be made automatically to the town firm. 
(2)  Tie bids involving only town firms or only out-of-town firms shall be resolved by the flip of a coin in the office of the procurement officer, witnessed by all interested parties. 
(c)  Cancellation of invitation for bids on request for proposals . An invitation for bids, a request for proposals, or other solicitation may be cancelled, or any or all bids or proposals may be rejected in whole or part as may be specified in the solicitation, when it is in the best interest of the town. The reasons for rejecting, supported with documentation sufficient to satisfy an external audit, shall be made a part of the contract file. 
(Code 1996, § 10-1-7) 
Sec. 10-1-8. - Award of contracts. 
    The town manager may reflect or approve bids and purchase agreements and award contracts in accordance with regulations, provided that contracts involving in excess of $5,000.00 shall be approved by the town council prior to award. 
(Code 1996, § 10-1-8) 
Sec. 10-1-9. - Department heads to authorize purchases under $500.00. 
    All purchases duly approved by the town council in the budget process that do not exceed $500.00 must be authorized by the appropriate department head or their designee prior to a purchase order number being issued. 
(Code 1996, § 10-1-9) 
Sec. 10-1-10. - Town manager to authorize purchases between $500.00 and $1,000.00. 
    All purchases duly approved by the town council in the budget process that exceed the authority of the department head but do not exceed $1,000.00 must be approved by the town manager or his designee prior to a purchase order number being issued. 
(Code 1996, § 10-1-10) 
Sec. 10-1-11. - Town council to approve purchases over $1,000.00; exceptions. 
    All purchases exceeding $1,000.00 must have the prior approval of the town council. This excludes only duly approved insurance payments, all utilities, emergency vehicle repairs, legal or professional fees, or any payment or refund ordered by an appropriate court having proper jurisdiction to issue such order. 
(Code 1996, § 10-1-11) 
Sec. 10-1-12. - Bids required for purchases exceeding $1,000.00. 
    All purchases exceeding $1,000.00 will be bid out and the lowest bid of acceptable quality shall be awarded. The town reserves the right to reject any and all bids. Local business shall have equal opportunity to bid on any purchase made by the town. 
(Code 1996, § 10-1-12) 
Sec. 10-1-13. - Purchase orders. 
(a)  All purchases made by the town shall have a purchase order number issued by the clerk-treasurer, excluding minor purchases made from petty cash funds and reoccurring purchases such as those itemized in section 10-1-11. 
(b)  Purchase orders shall contain the name of the business, description of item to be purchased, amount to be spent, approved budget line item number and person authorizing the purchase. The clerk-treasurer shall maintain a purchase order book and appropriately record all purchases made by the town. 
(Code 1996, § 10-1-13) 
CHAPTER 2. - PROCUREMENT REGULATIONS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Political subdivisions required to develop and adopt procurement laws, S.C. Code 1976, § 11-35-50. 

Sec. 10-2-1. - Town procurement regulations. 
    These regulations issued by the town manager, establish policies, procedures and guidelines relating to the procurement, management, control, and disposal of supplies, services, information technology and construction, as applicable, under the authority of the town procurement code. 
(Code 1996, § 10-2-1) 
Sec. 10-2-2. - Department heads may develop specifications and receive bids. 
    The town manager may designate, in writing, the authority to certain department heads to develop their own specifications and handle bidding procedures as outlined in these regulations. The term "procurement officer," as used in these regulations, shall mean the purchasing agent or any person duly authorized to handle a procurement. 
(Code 1996, § 10-2-2) 
Sec. 10-2-3. - Competitive sealed bidding. 
(a)  The invitation for bids . The invitation for bids by newspaper or by mail invitation to selective suppliers shall be used to initiate a competitive sealed bid procurement and shall include the following: 
(1)  Instructions and information to bidders concerning the bid submission requirements, including the time and date set for receipt of bids, the individual to whom the bid is to be submitted, the address of the office to which bids are to be delivered, the maximum time for bid acceptance by the town and any other special information; 
(2)  The purchase description, evaluation factors, delivery or performance schedule, and such inspection and acceptance requirements as are not included in the purchase description; 
(3)  The contract terms and conditions, including warranty and bonding or other security requirements, as applicable; and 
(4)  Instructions to bidders to visibly mark as confidential each part of their bid which they consider to be proprietary information. Bidding time will be set to provide bidders a reasonable time to prepare their bids.
